## Pass 4 — granular multi-dimension whole-repo sweep (verified)

A whole-repo re-hunt with **78 focused finders** (one per file × lens — code-logic/correctness, docstring+comment accuracy, test-masking, doc example/prose — plus 3 cross-file specialists on the TimeVaryingInputs method family, date arithmetic, and cache/MPI collectives), each deduped against all prior passes, with **one adversarial refuter per candidate**. 330 agents, 0 errors, ~35 min, 6.2M tokens; no Julia executed. **187 unique findings survived** verification (123 high-confidence, 64 medium). Medium-confidence items are marked _(med)_ — treat as strong leads.

| Location | bug | perf | doc-error | typo | grammar | style | total |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| SRC | 8 | 1 | 24 | 6 | 12 | 6 | **57** |
| EXT | 6 | 6 | 19 | 8 | 9 | 8 | **56** |
| DOCS | 2 | 0 | 15 | 6 | 27 | 1 | **51** |
| TEST | 7 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | 14 | **23** |
| **Total** | **23** | **7** | **58** | **21** | **49** | **29** | **187** |

### ⭐ Highest-impact (Pass 4 — bugs & performance)

- ⭐ **`docs/src/datahandling.md:181`** `[bug]` — `compose_function` is passed as a bare positional argument, not a keyword argument, so this example errors with a MethodError. **Evidence:** The call ends with `... file_reader_kwargs = (; ...), compose_function)`. There is no semicolon before `compose_function`, so Julia treats the bare identifier as a 4th positional argument. But `DataHandler(file_paths, varnames, target_space::AbstractSpace; ...)` (ext/DataHandlingExt.jl:201-215) accepts only 3 positional args, with `compose_function` being a keyword. Passing a 4th positional gives a MethodError. The `(; x)` keyword shorthand requires a semicolon. **Fix:** Write it as a keyword argument: `compose_function = compose_function`, or insert a semicolon before it so the shorthand applies (`...; compose_function`).
- ⭐ **`docs/src/regridders.md:53`** `[bug]` — TempestRegridder example passes wrong positional args and omits the required regrid_dir keyword. **Evidence:** The real constructor is `TempestRegridder(target_space, varname, input_file; regrid_dir, mono=true)` (ext/TempestRegridderExt.jl:67-73). The doc call `Regridders.TempestRegridder(target_space, "regrid_output", "u", "era5_example.nc")` passes 4 positional arguments where only 3 exist, so "regrid_output" binds to `varname`, "u" binds to `input_file`, "era5_example.nc" has no parameter, and the required keyword `regrid_dir` is never supplied. This is a MethodError, not a working example. **Fix:** reg = Regridders.TempestRegridder(target_space, "u", "era5_example.nc"; regrid_dir = "regrid_output")
- ⭐ **`ext/DataHandlingExt.jl:305`** `[bug]` — available_times uses the raw start_date, which may be a Date, and DateTime .- Date has no method in Dates, so constructing a time-varying DataHandler with a Date start_date throws a MethodError. **Evidence:** The constructor signature explicitly allows a Date: `start_date::Union{Dates.DateTime, Dates.Date} = Dates.DateTime(1979, 1, 1)` (L205). At L305, `available_times = period_to_seconds_float.(available_dates .- start_date)` broadcasts subtraction where `available_dates` is `AbstractArray{Dates.DateTime}` (struct field DATES, L54) and `start_date` is still the raw argument. Julia's Dates only defines same-type TimeType subtraction (DateTime-DateTime, Date-Date, Time-Time); there is no `-(::DateTime, ::Date)` method, so the element-wise `DateTime - Date` throws MethodError whenever `available_dates` is non-empty. The Date->DateTime conversion is applied only at L384 (`Dates.DateTime(start_date)`) for the struct field, which is too late to help L305. Static (empty-dates) files avoid it, but any time-varying input with a Date start_date breaks at construction. This is a DateTime/Date coercion gap in exactly the advertised code path. **Fix:** Normalize the argument to a DateTime before it is used arithmetically, e.g. add `start_date = Dates.DateTime(start_date)` immediately after the deprecated-kwargs block (before L305), and then pass `start_date` (already a DateTime) to the struct at L384. This keeps L305 and L384 consistent and makes the documented Date support actually work.
- ⭐ **`ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl:323`** `[bug]` — regrid! calls push! on a caller-supplied dimension vector, which crashes for range / non-resizable AbstractVector inputs that the method signature explicitly allows. **Evidence:** The signature is `dimensions::NTuple{N, AbstractVector{FT}}` (line 291), and `regrid` handles this same case safely by materializing every dimension with `FT.(dim)` -> a fresh Vector (line 211). But `regrid!` uses the input directly: `dimensions = deepcopy(dimensions)` preserves the input's concrete type, then `lon = dimensions[lon_dim_idx]; push!(lon, last(lon) + dlon)` (lines 320-323). `deepcopy` of a `StepRangeLen` is still a `StepRangeLen`, which has no `push!` method. Failing input: `Regridders.regrid!(out, reg, data, (0f0:1f0:359f0, lat))` with the default Periodic longitude BC. That range is equispaced and `359 - 0 + 1 = 360`, so `lon_oncell` is true (lines 305-312) and `push!(0f0:1f0:359f0, 360f0)` throws a MethodError. Ranges are the most natural equispaced/360-spanning longitude input, i.e. exactly the case that triggers this branch. **Fix:** Materialize the longitude dimension to a mutable Vector before mutating, e.g. replace lines 320-323 with `dimensions = Base.setindex(dimensions, vcat(dimensions[lon_dim_idx], last(dimensions[lon_dim_idx]) + (dimensions[lon_dim_idx][2] - dimensions[lon_dim_idx][1])), lon_dim_idx)`, or do `dimensions = map(collect, dimensions)` before the `push!`.
- ⭐ **`ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl:205`** `[bug]` — Dataset lifecycle reference-counts by a Set of varnames, not by reader count, so two readers sharing the same file AND varname cause a premature close (use-after-close) or a KeyError on close. **Evidence:** OPEN_NCFILES maps file_paths -> (dataset, Set{String} of varnames) (L17-18). On construction, a second NCFileReader for the same file_paths gets the existing tuple from get! (L132-139) and push!(open_varnames, varname) at L141 is a NO-OP when the Set already contains that varname (Set dedups). So two readers with identical file_paths+varname share one NCDataset and one Set entry {varname}. In Base.close, L205 pop!(open_variables, file_reader.varname) then L206-209 close the shared dataset and delete the OPEN_NCFILES entry once the Set empties. Closing reader1 therefore empties {varname}, closes the NCDataset, and deletes the key while reader2 still holds file_reader.dataset pointing at the now-closed dataset -> any FileReaders.read(reader2, ...) (L254/L260) operates on a closed NCDataset, and close(reader2) silently no-ops via the haskey guard at L201-202. A variant is a hard crash: with a third reader on a different varname keeping the Set non-empty (e.g. r1,r2 = (fileX,varA), r3 = (fileX,varB); Set={varA,varB}), close(r1) pops varA -> {varB}, then close(r2) runs pop!(open_variables, "varA") on a Set that no longer contains varA -> KeyError. The close-ordering test (test/file_readers.jl:46-53) only exercises two DIFFERENT varnames, so this is uncovered. This is exactly the shared-dataset use case the module comment (L11-16) and L132 finding describe. **Fix:** Reference-count by the number of live readers, not by distinct varnames: store a per-reader count (e.g. an Int, or a Dict{String,Int} / Accumulator keyed by varname) in the OPEN_NCFILES value and only NCDatasets.close + delete! when the total reader count reaches zero. Alternatively track distinct reader object identities. Also guard the pop! (L205) so a varname already removed does not throw.
- ⭐ **`ext/TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl:366`** `[bug]` — 23D NearestNeighbor evaluation crashes when the requested time equals the last available date, because next_date errors; the exact-date guard present in the LinearInterpolation sibling (and handled by searchsortednearest in the 0D sibling) is missing here. **Evidence:** In evaluate!(dest, itp::InterpolatingTimeVaryingInput23D, time, ::NearestNeighbor) the non-periodic path unconditionally evaluates both neighbors: `date0, date1 = previous_date(itp.data_handler, time), next_date(itp.data_handler, time)` (L365-366). For time == available_dates[end], next_date (ext/DataHandlingExt.jl:561-569) takes the `date in available_dates` branch and computes index = searchsortedfirst(...) + 1 = length+1, then hits `index > length(...) && error("Date $date is after available dates")`. With the default Throw BC, the main entry (L209-210) treats the last date as in-range (no error) and forwards here, so evaluating at exactly the final data time crashes. This is reachable through the ordinary Number API too (L227-242 converts a number time to that date). The sibling members all handle this in-range boundary correctly: 23D LinearInterpolation guards it at L416 (`if time in DataHandling.available_dates(itp.data_handler) ... regridded_snapshot!(dest, itp.data_handler, time)`), and 0D NearestNeighbor uses searchsortednearest (ext/TimeVaryingInputs0DExt.jl:185) whose L16-17 branch returns length(a) for the last element -> vals[end]. So 23D NearestNeighbor is the only member of the family that mishandles the last-date case. Distinct from the already-reported L358 finding, which concerns the PeriodicCalendar interior, not the non-periodic exact-last-date path. **Fix:** Add the same exact-date guard used by LinearInterpolation before computing the neighbors, e.g. at the top of the non-periodic block: `if time in DataHandling.available_dates(itp.data_handler); regridded_snapshot!(dest, itp.data_handler, time); return nothing; end`. (Equivalently, clamp next_date's index to the last available index.)
- ⭐ **`src/ClimaArtifacts.jl:230`** `[bug]` — Rank-divergent deadlock on artifact-download failure: in the variable-name branch the root runs the first _artifact_str inside a rethrowing try/catch and can exit the macro before reaching the collective barrier, leaving all non-root ranks blocked at it forever. **Evidence:** In the variable-name branch, only the root runs the first _artifact_str: if isnothing(context) || iamroot(context) (L205-206) wraps the call in a try/catch that RETHROWS on failure (L219-227, including the reworded 'too large' ErrorException at L221-223). Non-root ranks skip that if-block and proceed to push! (L229) and then the collective barrier at L230-231 (isnothing(context) || barrier(context)). If root's download fails, root unwinds out of the whole quoted expression via the rethrow and never executes L230-231, so it never enters the barrier; the non-root ranks that already reached L230-231 block on it indefinitely -> MPI hang instead of a clean failure. This is precisely the rank-divergent early-exit-past-a-collective pattern (root reaches the collective on the success path but not on the error path). (The constant-string branch has no barrier at all -- separately reported at L149 -- so it races rather than deadlocks.) **Fix:** Ensure every rank reaches the barrier regardless of the root's success: e.g. move the root-only first _artifact_str into a try/finally (or catch-and-flag) so barrier(context) at L230-231 always runs on all ranks, and after the barrier have root re-raise / all ranks cooperatively error (or call ClimaComms abort) so a download failure fails the run cleanly instead of hanging.
- ⭐ **`src/DataStructures.jl:277`** `[bug]` — Priority-vector key removal uses `!=` (i.e. `==`) while the backing `Dict` compares keys with `isequal`/`hash`, so for any key type where `==` and `isequal` disagree the priority vector desyncs from the cache. **Evidence:** `_update_priority!` does `filter!(k -> k != key, cache.priority)`, and the same `k != key` pattern is used in `pop!` (L236, L242) and `delete!` (L253). But `LRUCache <: AbstractDict` and `cache.cache::Dict` matches keys via `isequal`/`hash`, not `==`. Concrete failure: `c = LRUCache{Float64,Int}(); c[0.0]=1; c[-0.0]=2`. Since `isequal(0.0,-0.0)==false`, the Dict now holds BOTH keys, but `_update_priority!(c,-0.0)` runs `filter!(k -> k != -0.0, [0.0])` where `0.0 != -0.0` is `false`, so it erroneously drops `0.0` from `priority`. Result: `cache.cache` has 2 entries while `priority` has 1 → `0.0` is untracked (never evictable, leaks) and `length(cache)` disagrees with the priority queue. NaN keys behave analogously (Dict treats NaN==NaN via isequal, but `NaN != key` is always true, so duplicate NaN entries accumulate in `priority`). **Fix:** Compare with the same relation the Dict uses: replace `k != key` with `!isequal(k, key)` at lines 236, 242, 253, and 277.
- ⭐ **`src/ITime.jl:82`** `[bug]` — Auto-period integer constructor silently overflows because it computes `1_000_000_000 * counter` before dividing, so counters above ~9.2e9 seconds wrap to a wrong (often negative) value. **Evidence:** `typeof(counter)(div(1_000_000_000 * counter, period_ns))` forms the intermediate `1_000_000_000 * counter` in Int64. For `ITime(10_000_000_000)` (1e10 s ~317 yr, no period given), the loop reaches Second and returns `div(1_000_000_000 * 10_000_000_000, 1_000_000_000)`; `1e9 * 1e10 = 1e19 > typemax(Int64)=9.223e18`, so the product wraps to -8446744073709551616 and the result is `ITime(-8446744073, Second(1))` instead of `ITime(10_000_000_000, Second(1))`. This directly contradicts the docstring (lines 21-22) claiming Int64 is usable to ~300 gigayears, and is asymmetric with the float sibling (line 200) whose `Int(t_int)` path cannot silently wrap (it would throw InexactError). The huge-counter tests (test/itime.jl:324,337,345,348,357) all pass an explicit `period=`, taking the line-64 early return, so this branch is untested. **Fix:** Avoid the 1e9 multiply. Since only >=1s periods are ever selected here (see next finding), compute the count as `typeof(counter)(div(counter, div(period_ns, 1_000_000_000)))`, which is exact and cannot overflow the counter's own range. (A fully general fix that keeps sub-second support would need widening, e.g. `div(widemul(1_000_000_000, counter), period_ns)` via Int128.)
- ⭐ **`src/OutputPathGenerator.jl:199`** `[bug]` — The 4-digit-only regex combined with lpad-to-4 silently breaks the counter once the 10000th output folder is reached, causing the counter to regress and reuse/overwrite an existing folder. **Evidence:** `name_rx = r"output_(\d\d\d\d)"` (L199, also L338) matches exactly four digits and is unanchored, while `lpad(next_counter, 4, "0")` (L240) only pads and never truncates. After `output_9999`, `next_counter` becomes 10000 and the folder created is `output_10000`. On the next run `match(name_rx, "output_10000")` captures the first four digits `"1000"`, so `counter = 1000`, `next_counter = 1001`, and `output_1001` (which already exists from an earlier run) is silently reused via `mkpath` — the counter runs backwards and the documented non-destructive guarantee (L74-75) is violated. The same capture bug corrupts `first(sort(existing_outputs, rev = true))` selection in the no-link branch and the walk in detect_restart_file. **Fix:** Use a variable-width, anchored capture consistent with the padding, e.g. `r"output_(\d+)"` (or `r"^output_(\d{4,})$"`), and widen the lpad width or otherwise keep the format and regex in sync.
- ⭐ **`src/OutputPathGenerator.jl:265`** `[bug]` — The junction-fallback symlink is not wrapped in the error_message mechanism, so if it throws it does so on root only, deadlocking the other MPI ranks at the following bcast. **Evidence:** The outer symlink at L256 is guarded by try/catch that converts any failure into `error_message` (per the L178-182 comment: root must not throw, or the other ranks hang). But the fallback `symlink(dest_active_link, active_link, dir_target = true)` at L265 is itself unguarded. Junctions can still fail (e.g. target on a network share, filesystem without junction support). When it throws, root raises inside the `if iamroot(context)` block and never reaches `error_message = bcast(context, error_message)` (L272); non-root ranks are already waiting in that bcast, so the whole job deadlocks — exactly the failure mode the error_message design was built to prevent. This is a different defect from the already-catalogued wrong-abspath-target bug on L264. **Fix:** Wrap the fallback call the same way, e.g. `try symlink(dest_active_link, active_link, dir_target = true) catch e2; error_message = string(e2) end`, so a junction failure is broadcast as an error instead of thrown only on root.
- ⭐ **`test/itime.jl:229`** `[bug]` — In the `mod` test block, line 229 uses the `%` operator instead of `mod`, verbatim-duplicating line 224 and leaving `mod(t6, t7)` untested. **Evidence:** Lines 226-228 test `mod(t1,t2)`, `mod(t3,t2)`, `mod(t4,t5)`, establishing the intent to exercise `Base.mod(::ITime,::ITime)` (src/ITime.jl:346) directly. Line 229 instead reads `@test t6 % t7 == ITime(1, period = Second(2))`, which is character-for-character identical to line 224 in the `%` block above. Since `%` merely forwards to `mod` (src/ITime.jl:358-360), line 229 re-tests the exact same call as line 224 and never invokes `mod(t6, t7)`. The `Second(2)`/period-2 case for the `mod` function name therefore has no coverage, and the line adds nothing over line 224. **Fix:** Change line 229 to `@test mod(t6, t7) == ITime(1, period = Second(2))` to match the pattern of lines 226-228 and actually test `mod` for the period-2 fixtures.
- ⭐ **`test/regridders.jl:444`** `[bug]` — The dimension-reversal equivalence assertion `result_wrong == result` is trivially true because the input data is all zeros, so it cannot detect a broken reversal. **Evidence:** `data_3D = zeros(size3D)` (line 402) is never filled. `result` (417-421) uses correctly-ordered dims with dim_increasing all true; `result_wrong` (437-441) uses `dimensions_wrongly_ordered = (reverse(lon), lat, z)` with `dim_increasing = (false, true, true)`. The comment (424-429) claims the test verifies that internally reversing the decreasing dimension AND the data slices (source ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl lines 210-220 do `reverse(FT.(dim))` and `reverse(data, dims=decreasing_indices)`) yields an identical result. But reversing all-zero data is a no-op and interpolating zeros always yields a zero field, so `result_wrong == result` holds regardless of whether the reversal logic is correct — the assertion masks any regression in that code path. Note the sibling 'incorrect dimensions' testset (lines 32-139) uses meaningful data (lat/lon/z values) for the same kind of comparison, which is why those catch real errors. **Fix:** Fill `data_3D` with a non-symmetric field that varies along the reversed dimension (e.g. `data_3D[i,:,:] .= lon[i]`) before regridding, so `result_wrong == result` actually exercises the dimension/data reversal.
- ⭐ **`test/space_varying_inputs.jl:61`** `[bug]` — Masking/tautological assertion: `field_of_structs.b == 2 .* field_of_structs.a` can never fail, so it never verifies that b was interpolated correctly. **Evidence:** The `Tmp{FT}` inner constructor (lines 52-55) hardcodes `b = a * 2`, and that inner constructor is the only way to build a `Tmp`. `SpaceVaryingInput` (ext/SpaceVaryingInputsExt.jl lines 118-123) builds each element via `DT(; args...)`, so for every point `b` is set to exactly `2*a`. Therefore `field_of_structs.b == 2 .* field_of_structs.a` holds by construction regardless of what the underlying interpolation produced — a regression in the interpolation of `a`/`b` would leave both wrong together and still pass. Unlike `a` (cross-checked against `field` at line 60, itself checked against ground truth `range(0.1,1.9,10)` at line 46) and `c` (checked against `range(0.15,2.85,10)` at lines 62-63), `b` has NO independent ground-truth check, so this component is effectively untested. **Fix:** Assert `b` against an independent expected value instead of against a derived quantity, e.g. `@test parent(field_of_structs.b)[:] ≈ AT(collect(range(FT(0.2), FT(3.8), 10)))` (2x the expected `a` values), which exercises both the interpolation and the constructor's `b = 2a` derivation.
- ⭐ **`test/time_varying_inputs.jl:291`** `[bug]` — The linear-interpolation value check evaluates the input at t=10 but compares against an expected value computed for t=0.1, so the assertion checks the wrong point. **Evidence:** Line 291 calls evaluate!(dest, input, ft_to_input(FT(10))), so dest holds the value at t=10. Since times = 0:0.5:100, t=10 is times[21], an exact node, so linear interp returns vals[21] = sin(10.0) (about -0.544). But lines 296-302 then compute index = searchsortedfirst(times, 0.1) and expected = linear interpolation at t=0.1 (about interp between sin(0)=0 and sin(0.5), ~0.096). Line 304 asserts Array(parent(dest))[1] ≈ expected, i.e. sin(10.0) ≈ interp@0.1, which is false. This is a distinct defect from the catalogued L293 `eltype(time)` guard bug: even after fixing that guard to `eltype(times)`, this assertion would fail because the evaluate time (10) does not match the time the expected value was computed for (0.1). **Fix:** Change ft_to_input(FT(10)) on line 291 to ft_to_input(FT(0.1)) so dest is evaluated at the same time the expected value (lines 296-302) is computed for.
- ⭐ **`ext/TimeVaryingInputs0DExt.jl:119`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — The ITime epoch-mismatch guard is unreachable, so differing-epoch inputs never hit its clear error and instead crash with a generic message from `promote`. **Evidence:** The `elseif` at line 118 is only entered when the line-109 `!all(t -> t.period == first(times).period && t.epoch == first(times).epoch, times)` is FALSE, i.e. every element already has the same period AND epoch as `first(times)`. Under that precondition `all(d -> d.epoch == first(times).epoch, times)` (line 119) is trivially TRUE, so its `error("...ITime(s) with differing epochs")` can never fire — it is dead code. The case it was meant to catch (equal periods but differing epochs) makes the line-109 `all` FALSE, routing it to `times = [promote(times...)...]` on line 117; `promote`/`find_common_epoch` in src/ITime.jl:259-277 then throws `error("Cannot find common epoch")` instead of the intended descriptive message. Failing input: `times = [ITime(0; period=Second(1), epoch=DateTime(2000)), ITime(1; period=Second(1), epoch=DateTime(2001))]` errors with "Cannot find common epoch", never reaching the guard. **Fix:** Restructure so the epoch check runs before/independently of the promote branch, e.g. first validate `eltype(times) <: ITime{<:Any,<:Any,Nothing} || all(d -> d.epoch == first(times).epoch, times) || error("...differing epochs")`, and only then promote to unify periods; remove the unreachable `elseif` body.
- ⭐ **`ext/TimeVaryingInputs0DExt.jl:161`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — `_time_range_target_time_dt` indexes `times[begin+1]` with no length guard, so a single-sample PeriodicCalendar input crashes at the first evaluate. **Evidence:** Line 161 does `dt = itp.times[begin + 1] - itp.times[begin]`. A one-element time series with `PeriodicCalendar()` passes the constructor because `isequispaced` returns `true` for `length(v) < 2` (src/Utils.jl:99), so no error is raised at build time; the first periodic `evaluate!` (reaching line 178 or 212) then throws `BoundsError` on `itp.times[begin+1]`. Relatedly, the constructor's `range = (times[begin], times[end])` on line 139 throws `BoundsError` for empty `times`/`vals` (empty arrays satisfy `issorted` and the equal-length check). **Fix:** Guard early with a clear message, e.g. require `length(times) >= 2` (or `>= 1`) in the constructor, and for the PeriodicCalendar single-sample case emit an explicit error rather than an out-of-range index.
- ⭐ **`src/DataStructures.jl:39`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — Constructor accepts `max_size <= 0` with no validation; with such a value the cache silently grows without bound because `_enforce_size!` empties `priority` before every insertion. **Evidence:** `LRUCache{K,V}(; max_size::Int = 128)` does not require `max_size >= 1`. `_enforce_size!` (L290) evicts when `length(cache.priority) > cache.max_size`, but it runs BEFORE the unconditional insert in `setindex!`/`get!`. With `max_size=0`: `c = LRUCache{Int,Int}(max_size=0); c[1]=1` → `_update_priority!` makes `priority=[1]`, `_enforce_size!` sees `1 > 0`, `popfirst!` empties `priority` and `delete!`s key 1 from the (still empty) dict, then `cache.cache[1]=1` inserts it anyway. Repeating `c[2]=2`, `c[3]=3`, ... leaves `priority` empty every time while `cache.cache` grows unboundedly — the exact opposite of a size-0 cache. **Fix:** Validate in the constructor, e.g. `max_size >= 1 || throw(ArgumentError("max_size must be >= 1"))`.
- ⭐ **`src/TimeVaryingInputs.jl:128`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — PeriodicCalendar constructor omits the documented guard requiring repeat_date when a period is provided, allowing an invalid object that fails obscurely downstream. **Evidence:** The inner constructor only checks `if period isa DatePeriod && period.value != 1 error(...) end` and then `return new{...}(period, repeat_date)`; it never validates that repeat_date is present when period is. The docstring explicitly states (line 88): "When provided a period, a `repeat_date` is required too." Thus `PeriodicCalendar(Dates.Month(1), nothing)` constructs successfully, then dispatches to `_time_range_dt_dt_e(itp, ::PeriodicCalendar)` (ext/TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl:272), which calls `bounding_dates(available_dates(itp.data_handler), repeat_date, period)` (ext line 277) with repeat_date === nothing, yielding an unclear failure in date arithmetic instead of a clear constructor error. **Fix:** After the existing period check add: `if !isnothing(period) && isnothing(repeat_date) error("A repeat_date is required when a period is provided") end` before `return new{...}(...)`.
- ⭐ **`src/Utils.jl:101`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — isequispaced computes dv with offset-aware `begin` indexing but then iterates absolute 1-based indices 2:length(v) under @inbounds, giving out-of-bounds reads and misaligned pairs for any non-1-based AbstractVector. **Evidence:** Line 100 uses `dv = v[begin + 1] - v[begin]` (offset-aware), but line 101-102 do `@inbounds for i in 2:length(v) ... abs(v[i] - v[i - 1] - dv)`. For an OffsetVector with axes 0:n-1, valid indices are 0..n-1, yet the loop reads i up to length(v)=n, so `v[n]` is out of bounds; @inbounds suppresses the BoundsError, yielding garbage/UB, and the pairs being differenced no longer correspond to the actual consecutive elements. Only a 1-based vector makes the two indexing styles agree. This is an internal inconsistency with the `begin` usage on line 100. **Fix:** Use consistent index-agnostic bounds, e.g. `first_i = firstindex(v); dv = v[first_i + 1] - v[first_i]; @inbounds for i in (first_i + 1):lastindex(v) ...`, or drop `begin` and index 1-based throughout.
- ⭐ **`test/regridders.jl:265`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — Periodic non-end-point error check uses minimum() instead of maximum(), so it passes if any single point matches even when every other point is wrong. **Evidence:** Line 265: `@test minimum(abs.(view(diff_coordinates, inds_not_ends))) ≈ 0.0`. The comment (256-258) and index filter `inds_not_ends` (261-264) establish the intent: at all longitudes other than +/-180, the regridded value must equal the coordinate (diff ~ 0). `minimum(abs.(...)) ≈ 0.0` only asserts the SMALLEST error is ~0, i.e. at least one non-end point matches; a systematic error at all other non-end points would still pass. The sibling function `check_lon_error` (234-249) correctly uses `maximum(abs.(...)) < tol`, and the +/-180 checks at 274/279 use `all(...)`, confirming the intended semantics is 'all', not 'any'. **Fix:** Use `maximum(abs.(view(diff_coordinates, inds_not_ends))) ≈ 0.0` (or `all(≈(0.0), abs.(view(diff_coordinates, inds_not_ends)))`) to require every non-end point to have ~0 error.
- ⭐ **`test/time_varying_inputs.jl:286`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — The block labeled 'Linear interpolation' actually evaluates the NearestNeighbor input at a node point, so the assertion passes for any method and never verifies linear interpolation. **Evidence:** The comment on line 278 labels this 'Linear interpolation', but `input` here is still the NearestNeighbor() input from line 169 (it is not reassigned to the default LinearInterpolation input until line 289, verified default at ext/TimeVaryingInputs0DExt.jl:88). Line 283 evaluates at time_to_input(times[10]), an exact node, where both NearestNeighbor and LinearInterpolation return vals[10]. Therefore @test Array(parent(dest))[1] == vals[10] (line 286) passes regardless of the interpolation method and does not test linear interpolation as the comment claims (masking). **Fix:** Move the `input = TimeVaryingInput(times, vals)` reassignment (line 289) above this block and/or evaluate at a non-node time (e.g. between two nodes) so the assertion actually distinguishes linear interpolation from nearest-neighbor; at minimum correct the misleading comment.
- ⭐ **`test/time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl:137`** `[bug]` _(med)_ — test_date's approximate-equality assertion cannot detect wrong date/period selection in the non-interpolable branch because the fixture data is globally linear and that branch's coefficient is derived from real-time differences, self-correcting any date choice. **Evidence:** The fixture data (line 99, `data = stack(map(t -> ones_array * t, times))`) makes value == time everywhere. In the source's non-interpolable branch (ext/time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl lines 361-366) coeff = (time - date_pre)/(date_post - date_pre) is computed from ACTUAL time differences, so dest = time(date_pre)*(1-coeff) + time(date_post)*coeff = time(target) EXACTLY for any finite date_pre != date_post that recursively resolve to their true linear values. I traced test_date(DateTime(1987,1,1)) (line 169) with the already-catalogued ext:348 bug (date_pre placed in period 1988 instead of 1986): coeff becomes ~1.013 and the result is still exactly time(target)=730 days, so `@test parent(dest) ≈ parent(expected)` passes. The same masking applies to the other else-branch cases at lines 172, 175, 178, which claim to verify left/right-of-interpolable-region date selection but verify only that no error is thrown. **Fix:** Use a fixture whose value depends non-linearly on the date/period (e.g. a distinct constant per available period, or a per-date label) so an incorrect date_pre/date_post yields a detectably wrong result; and/or assert the selected date_pre/date_post directly in the non-interpolable cases.
- ⭐ **`ext/TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl:277`** `[perf]` — PeriodicCalendar (with period) recomputes constant bounding dates via an allocating O(N) filter on every evaluate!. **Evidence:** `_time_range_dt_dt_e(itp, ::PeriodicCalendar)` calls `bounding_dates(available_dates(itp.data_handler), repeat_date, period)` (line 277) on every timestep, because it is reached through `_interpolation_times_periodic_calendar` from both the NearestNeighbor (line 349) and LinearInterpolation (line 395) evaluate! hot paths. `bounding_dates` (Utils.jl:293) runs `filter(date -> period_start <= date <= period_end, dates)`, which heap-allocates a new vector and scans all dates O(N), plus beginning/endofperiod arithmetic (lines 287-288) — all producing values (date_init, date_end, dt, dt_e) that are constant for the lifetime of the input. The sibling PeriodicCalendar{Nothing} branch (line 263) is similarly wasteful, recomputing DataHandling.dt (which re-runs the O(N) isequispaced check, DataHandlingExt.jl:430) each call. **Fix:** Compute date_init/date_end/dt/dt_e once at construction (store them in the InterpolatingTimeVaryingInput23D struct or a cached field) and read them in _time_range_dt_dt_e instead of recomputing bounding_dates/dt on every evaluate!.
- ⭐ **`src/Utils.jl:293`** `[perf]` — bounding_dates uses filter (O(N) scan + fresh allocation) on every evaluate! call for 23D PeriodicCalendar inputs, even though dates is sorted and only the first/last in-range element is needed. **Evidence:** Line 293: `dates_in_period = filter(date -> period_start <= date <= period_end, dates)`, then `first`/`last` on line 299. bounding_dates is called per-timestep: evaluate!(23D, PeriodicCalendar) -> _interpolation_times_periodic_calendar (ext/TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl:350,396) -> _time_range_dt_dt_e (line 335) -> bounding_dates (line 277), with no caching. `filter` allocates a whole new vector and walks the entire dates array O(N) on each call. The extension explicitly documents 'We can assume that dates are sorted', so first/last of the filter are just the smallest/largest in-range dates, obtainable in O(log N) with no allocation. This is a hot-path (not constructor) cost. **Fix:** Replace the filter+first/last with a binary search: `lo = searchsortedfirst(dates, period_start); hi = searchsortedlast(dates, period_end); hi > lo || error("$(target_date) not in given dates for given period"); return dates[lo], dates[hi]`. This is O(log N) and non-allocating; `hi > lo` preserves the existing >=2-dates requirement.
- ⭐ **`ext/DataHandlingExt.jl:544`** `[perf]` _(med)_ — `previous_date`/`next_date` (and their `previous_time`/`next_time` counterparts) do an O(N) `in` scan followed by an O(log N) `searchsortedfirst` on the same sorted array, doubling work in a per-timestep path. **Evidence:** L544 `if date in data_handler.available_dates` is O(N), then L545/L547 call `searchsortedfirst(data_handler.available_dates, date)` (O(log N)) regardless. The identical redundant pattern appears in `next_date` (L562), `previous_time` (L497), and `next_time` (L522). `previous_date`/`next_date` are called once each per LinearInterpolation `evaluate!` (TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl L419-420), so each timestep pays two O(N) scans that are entirely avoidable since the array is sorted. **Fix:** Compute `index = searchsortedfirst(available_dates, date)` once and derive membership from `index <= length(available_dates) && available_dates[index] == date`, adjusting `index` by -1 (previous) or +1 (next) accordingly; drop the separate `in` scan in all four functions.
- ⭐ **`ext/DataHandlingExt.jl:597`** `[perf]` _(med)_ — Per-timestep `regridded_snapshot` does an O(N) linear `in` membership scan of the sorted `available_dates` on every call, including cache hits. **Evidence:** `date in data_handler.available_dates` (L597) is `∈` on an AbstractVector, which is a linear O(N) scan; `available_dates` is guaranteed sorted (it is used with `searchsortedfirst` elsewhere). This runs before the `get!` on L604, so even fully cached snapshots pay O(N); LinearInterpolation calls `regridded_snapshot!` twice per timestep (TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl L423-424), so this is 2 O(N) scans/timestep over a dates vector that can be thousands of entries. **Fix:** Use an O(log N) membership test on the sorted array, e.g. `idx = searchsortedfirst(available_dates, date); (idx <= length(available_dates) && available_dates[idx] == date) || error(...)`, and/or move the availability check inside the `get!` closure so cache hits skip it entirely.
- ⭐ **`ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl:249`** `[perf]` _(med)_ — Dated read does an O(N) linear scan with findall (which also heap-allocates a Vector) to locate a date, even though available_dates is guaranteed sorted, so O(log N) searchsorted applies. **Evidence:** Line 249: `index = findall(d -> d == date, file_reader.available_dates)` scans the entire vector and allocates a `Vector{Int}` on every read; the constructor already enforces `issorted(available_dates)` (line 158). For a multi-year hourly dataset (tens of thousands of dates) every per-timestep read pays O(N) plus an allocation instead of O(log N). **Fix:** Use `idx = searchsortedfirst(file_reader.available_dates, date); (idx <= length(file_reader.available_dates) && file_reader.available_dates[idx] == date) || error("Problem with date $date ...")` and use `idx` directly (no allocation, O(log N)). If strict duplicate detection is still wanted, additionally compare `searchsortedlast`.
- ⭐ **`ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl:254`** `[perf]` _(med)_ — The `var = file_reader.dataset[file_reader.varname]` local is used only for its dimnames and then discarded; the same dataset indexing is repeated at line 260, doubling the CFVariable lookup/wrapper construction per read. **Evidence:** Line 254 binds `var`, but line 260 re-evaluates `file_reader.dataset[file_reader.varname][slicer...]` from scratch instead of reusing `var`. `dataset[varname]` on an NCDataset/MFDataset performs a lookup and constructs a fresh CFVariable wrapper, so this runs twice on every per-timestep read. **Fix:** Reuse the existing binding: `return file_reader.preprocess_func.(var[slicer...])`.
- ⭐ **`ext/time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl:183`** `[perf]` _(med)_ — maximum([...]) / minimum([...]) over two scalars allocate throwaway 2-element arrays on every evaluate! call. **Evidence:** `maximum([minimum(dates_period_left), minimum(dates_period_right_moved_to_left)])` (line 183) and the mirrored `minimum([...])` (line 187) each build a 2-element `Vector{DateTime}` array literal just to reduce two values. These run per-timestep via `_interpolable_range`; the array literals are pure allocation overhead. **Fix:** Use the binary scalar forms `max(minimum(dates_period_left), min_right)` and `min(maximum(dates_period_left), max_right)`, which allocate nothing.

### SRC (Pass 4)

#### `src/ClimaArtifacts.jl`
- **L230** `[bug]` — Rank-divergent deadlock on artifact-download failure: in the variable-name branch the root runs the first _artifact_str inside a rethrowing try/catch and can exit the macro before reaching the collective barrier, leaving all non-root ranks blocked at it forever. **Fix:** Ensure every rank reaches the barrier regardless of the root's success: e.g. move the root-only first _artifact_str into a try/finally (or catch-and-flag) so barrier(context) at L230-231 always runs on all ranks, and after the barrier have root re-raise / all ranks cooperatively error (or call ClimaComms abort) so a download failure fails the run cleanly instead of hanging.
- **L105** `[doc-error]` — Copy-pasted comment contradicts the branch it sits in: it claims the name is NOT a string / work is done at runtime, but this is the constant-string compile-time branch. **Fix:** Delete the misplaced lines 105-106 (or replace them with a comment describing the constant-string case), leaving the identical comment only in the `else` branch at lines 172-174.
- **L32** `[grammar]` — Subject-verb / plural agreement error in the docstring: singular "the other" paired with plural verb "wait". **Fix:** Change "while the other wait" to "while the others wait".
- **L115** `[style]` _(med)_ — In the constant-string branch the runtime artifact_slash_lookup is redundant work: two of its three outputs are unused and the third is already available as a compile-time constant. **Fix:** In the constant-string branch, replace `push!(ACCESSED_ARTIFACTS, artifact_name)` (line 149) with `push!(ACCESSED_ARTIFACTS, $(artifact_name))` and delete the now-unused runtime `local artifact_name, artifact_path_tail, hash = artifact_slash_lookup(...)` (lines 115-121) and `local platform` (line 114).
- **L128** `[style]` _(med)_ — The result of the first (root-only) _artifact_str call is bound to a local `artifact_path` that is never read, in both branches. **Fix:** Call `Base.invokelatest(JuliaArtifacts._artifact_str, ...)` without binding its result (or add a comment noting the value is intentionally discarded to trigger the download) at both line 128 and line 208.

#### `src/DataHandling.jl`
- **L20** `[doc-error]` _(med)_ — Docstring says the DataHandler "contains a `FileReaders`, a `Regridders`" (module names, singular "a"), but the struct holds a dictionary of file readers (one per variable) in field `file_readers` and a single `regridder`. **Fix:** Reword to "contains a collection of `FileReader`s (field `file_readers`, one per variable), a `Regridder` (field `regridder`), and other metadata".
- **L21** `[doc-error]` _(med)_ — Docstring references the nonexistent symbol `ClimaCore.Space`; the actual target-space type is `ClimaCore.Spaces.AbstractSpace` (module is `ClimaCore.Spaces`, plural). **Fix:** Change `ClimaCore.Space` to `ClimaCore.Spaces.AbstractSpace` (or `ClimaCore.Spaces`).
- **L34** `[doc-error]` _(med)_ — Module docstring says time<->date conversion uses a "reference date and simulation starting time", but the current DataHandler API uses a single `start_date`; the two-parameter model (`reference_date` + `t_start`) is deprecated. **Fix:** Reword to reference the single `start_date` keyword, e.g. "Conversion between time and date is performed using the `start_date` provided to the `DataHandler` (time is measured in seconds relative to `start_date`)."
- **L14** `[grammar]` _(med)_ — Stray comma before "and" in the two-item list "`FileReaders`, and `Regridders`". **Fix:** Remove the comma: "(chiefly `FileReaders` and `Regridders`)".

#### `src/DataStructures.jl`
- **L39** `[bug]` _(med)_ — Constructor accepts `max_size <= 0` with no validation; with such a value the cache silently grows without bound because `_enforce_size!` empties `priority` before every insertion. **Fix:** Validate in the constructor, e.g. `max_size >= 1 || throw(ArgumentError("max_size must be >= 1"))`.
- **L277** `[bug]` — Priority-vector key removal uses `!=` (i.e. `==`) while the backing `Dict` compares keys with `isequal`/`hash`, so for any key type where `==` and `isequal` disagree the priority vector desyncs from the cache. **Fix:** Compare with the same relation the Dict uses: replace `k != key` with `!isequal(k, key)` at lines 236, 242, 253, and 277.
- **L108** `[doc-error]` — `==` docstring signature uses `V2` for cache1's value type parameter; the real method uses `V1`. **Fix:** Change the docstring signature to `==(cache1::LRUCache{K1, V1}, cache2::LRUCache{K2, V2})`.
- **L148** `[doc-error]` — `Base.get` (Callable) docstring signature names the callable `default`, but the method's argument is `f` and the docstring body itself references `f()`. **Fix:** Change the signature to `Base.get(f::Callable, cache::LRUCache{K, V}, key::K)`.
- **L194** `[doc-error]` — `Base.empty` docstring signature `key_type::DataType=K, value_type::DataType=V` contradicts the actual dispatch: a single positional type argument is treated as `value_type`, not `key_type`. **Fix:** Document the two real methods explicitly, e.g. `Base.empty(cache::LRUCache{K, V}, value_type::DataType = V)` and `Base.empty(cache::LRUCache{K, V}, key_type::DataType, value_type::DataType)`.
- **L258** `[doc-error]` — `Base.merge` docstring signature is indented 3 spaces instead of the 4 required for a Markdown/Documenter code block, so it will not render as a code block. **Fix:** Add one leading space so the signature is indented 4 spaces to match the other docstrings.
- **L249** `[typo]` — Missing space before `cache` in the `Base.delete!` docstring. **Fix:** Add a space: 'if it is in `cache`'.
- **L200** `[grammar]` — Missing 'be' in the `Base.empty` docstring prose. **Fix:** Change to 'and `key_type` is assumed to be the key type of `cache`.'
- **L252** `[style]` — `delete!` assigns the return of `delete!(cache.cache, key)` to a misleadingly-named, unused local (dead assignment copy-pasted from `pop!`). **Fix:** Drop the binding: `delete!(cache.cache, key)`.

#### `src/FileReaders.jl`
- **L10** `[grammar]` _(med)_ — Module docstring uses singular 'NCFileReader' where a plural is required by the sentence, and it refers to the type/reader as a count noun ('multiple ... reader'). **Fix:** Change to 'This allows multiple NCFileReaders to share the underlying file without overhead.'

#### `src/ITime.jl`
- **L82** `[bug]` — Auto-period integer constructor silently overflows because it computes `1_000_000_000 * counter` before dividing, so counters above ~9.2e9 seconds wrap to a wrong (often negative) value. **Fix:** Avoid the 1e9 multiply. Since only >=1s periods are ever selected here (see next finding), compute the count as `typeof(counter)(div(counter, div(period_ns, 1_000_000_000)))`, which is exact and cannot overflow the counter's own range. (A fully general fix that keeps sub-second support would need widening, e.g. `div(widemul(1_000_000_000, counter), period_ns)` via Int128.)
- **L21** `[doc-error]` — Overflow formula in the type docstring is inverted: it uses (1 Second / dt) where it should be (dt / 1 Second). **Fix:** Replace `(1 Second / dt)` with `(dt / 1 Second)` in both the Int32 and Int64 expressions.
- **L208** `[grammar]` _(med)_ — Ungrammatical clause "instead of reconstruct the string" in the Base.show comment (distinct from the catalogued 'my'->'by' typo on L209). **Fix:** Change to "...so instead we reconstruct the string from the type name and the value...".
- **L284** `[grammar]` — Subject-verb disagreement ("Multiplication ... return") and a missing article ("and float"). **Fix:** Change to "Multiplication between an `ITime` and a float returns an `ITime` whose counter is ...".
- **L73** `[style]` — The Millisecond/Microsecond/Nanosecond entries in the integer constructor's `potential_periods` are unreachable dead code, unlike the identical list in the float constructor where they are live. **Fix:** Drop the sub-second entries from the integer constructor's `potential_periods` (Week..Second suffice), or add a comment noting they are unreachable for integer counters.

#### `src/OnlineLogging.jl`
- **L64** `[doc-error]` — The `_update!` docstring refers to a nonexistent `update!` function when describing what the function tracks. **Fix:** Change `update!` to `_update!` on line 64.
- **L90** `[typo]` _(med)_ — Comment names `_update` (missing the bang), which is not a real symbol; the function is `_update!`. **Fix:** Change `_update` to `_update!` on line 90.
- **L227** `[style]` _(med)_ — `isapprox(seconds, 0)` is not an approximate check — with the default `atol=0` it is effectively an exact `seconds == 0` test. **Fix:** Use an explicit tolerance if approximate-zero is intended, e.g. `isapprox(seconds, 0; atol = 1e-9) && return "0 seconds"`, or make the exact intent obvious with `seconds == 0 && ...`.
- **L241** `[style]` _(med)_ — Redundant no-op round-trip: multiplying by 86400 then dividing by 86400 makes `simulated_days_per_day` identically equal to `simulated_seconds_per_second`. **Fix:** Drop the cancelling operations: `simulated_days_per_day = simulated_seconds_per_second` (and remove the unused `simulated_seconds_per_day` line), or compute `simulated_years_per_day = simulated_seconds_per_second / 365.25` directly while keeping `simulated_days_per_day = simulated_seconds_per_second` for the sdpd branch.

#### `src/OutputPathGenerator.jl`
- **L199** `[bug]` — The 4-digit-only regex combined with lpad-to-4 silently breaks the counter once the 10000th output folder is reached, causing the counter to regress and reuse/overwrite an existing folder. **Fix:** Use a variable-width, anchored capture consistent with the padding, e.g. `r"output_(\d+)"` (or `r"^output_(\d{4,})$"`), and widen the lpad width or otherwise keep the format and regex in sync.
- **L265** `[bug]` — The junction-fallback symlink is not wrapped in the error_message mechanism, so if it throws it does so on root only, deadlocking the other MPI ranks at the following bcast. **Fix:** Wrap the fallback call the same way, e.g. `try symlink(dest_active_link, active_link, dir_target = true) catch e2; error_message = string(e2) end`, so a junction failure is broadcast as an error instead of thrown only on root.
- **L19** `[doc-error]` — maybe_wait_filesystem docstring signature marks keyword arguments as positional (comma after `path` should be a semicolon). **Fix:** Change the comma after `path` to a semicolon in the docstring: `maybe_wait_filesystem(context, path; check_func = ispath, sleep_time = 0.1, max_attempts = 10)`.
- **L111** `[doc-error]` — The generate_output_path docstrings state a context default of nothing and show positional arguments, contradicting the actual keyword-only signature whose default is ClimaComms.context(). **Fix:** Update the docstring signatures to use keyword syntax and `context = ClimaComms.context()` to match the code (the same positional/keyword mismatch also affects the maybe_wait_filesystem docstring at L18-22).
- **L168** `[doc-error]` — generate_output_path(::ActiveLinkStyle,...) docstring shows `context` as a positional argument, but it is a keyword argument. **Fix:** Replace the comma before `context` with a semicolon: `generate_output_path(::ActiveLinkStyle, output_path; context = nothing)`.
- **L316** `[doc-error]` — The detect_restart_file docstring documents a keyword argument name that does not exist in the function. **Fix:** Rename the documented argument from `output_dir_style` to `style`.
- **L25** `[grammar]` — maybe_wait_filesystem docstring sentence is missing a connector word, producing a run-on/ungrammatical clause. **Fix:** Insert 'when' (or 'after'): 'might need some time to catch up when a file/folder is created/removed.'
- **L90** `[grammar]` — Garbled word order in the ActiveLinkStyle example: 'will a create new directory'. **Fix:** Reorder to 'will create a new directory'.

#### `src/Utils.jl`
- **L101** `[bug]` _(med)_ — isequispaced computes dv with offset-aware `begin` indexing but then iterates absolute 1-based indices 2:length(v) under @inbounds, giving out-of-bounds reads and misaligned pairs for any non-1-based AbstractVector. **Fix:** Use consistent index-agnostic bounds, e.g. `first_i = firstindex(v); dv = v[first_i + 1] - v[first_i]; @inbounds for i in (first_i + 1):lastindex(v) ...`, or drop `begin` and index 1-based throughout.
- **L293** `[perf]` — bounding_dates uses filter (O(N) scan + fresh allocation) on every evaluate! call for 23D PeriodicCalendar inputs, even though dates is sorted and only the first/last in-range element is needed. **Fix:** Replace the filter+first/last with a binary search: `lo = searchsortedfirst(dates, period_start); hi = searchsortedlast(dates, period_end); hi > lo || error("$(target_date) not in given dates for given period"); return dates[lo], dates[hi]`. This is O(log N) and non-allocating; `hi > lo` preserves the existing >=2-dates requirement.
- **L62** `[doc-error]` — isequispaced documents tol default as sqrt(eps(eltype(v))) but the actual default falls back to eps() for non-float element types **Fix:** Document the conditional default, e.g. "`sqrt(eps(eltype(v)))` for floating-point element types, otherwise `eps()`".
- **L122** `[doc-error]` — wrap_time docstring introduces its examples with 'With `extend_past_t_end = false`:', but wrap_time has no such parameter. **Fix:** Delete the `With `extend_past_t_end = false`:` line (or reword it so it does not imply wrap_time accepts an extend_past_t_end argument).
- **L157** `[doc-error]` — beginningofperiod docstring signature restricts date to ::Date but the method accepts Union{Date, DateTime} **Fix:** Change the docstring signature to `beginningofperiod(date::Union{Date, DateTime}, period::DatePeriod)` to match the method.
- **L54** `[typo]` — isequispaced docstring signature has unbalanced parentheses (missing the function's closing paren) **Fix:** Add the missing closing paren: `isequispaced(v; tol::Real = sqrt(eps(eltype(v))))`.
- **L400** `[typo]` _(med)_ — sort_by_creation_time example has a misplaced semicolon inside the map(...) call so output suppression is broken **Fix:** Move the semicolon outside the call: `files = map(f -> joinpath(basedir, f), ["file3.txt", "file1.txt", "file2.txt"]);`.

### EXT (Pass 4)

#### `ext/DataHandlingExt.jl`
- **L305** `[bug]` — available_times uses the raw start_date, which may be a Date, and DateTime .- Date has no method in Dates, so constructing a time-varying DataHandler with a Date start_date throws a MethodError. **Fix:** Normalize the argument to a DateTime before it is used arithmetically, e.g. add `start_date = Dates.DateTime(start_date)` immediately after the deprecated-kwargs block (before L305), and then pass `start_date` (already a DateTime) to the struct at L384. This keeps L305 and L384 consistent and makes the documented Date support actually work.
- **L544** `[perf]` _(med)_ — `previous_date`/`next_date` (and their `previous_time`/`next_time` counterparts) do an O(N) `in` scan followed by an O(log N) `searchsortedfirst` on the same sorted array, doubling work in a per-timestep path. **Fix:** Compute `index = searchsortedfirst(available_dates, date)` once and derive membership from `index <= length(available_dates) && available_dates[index] == date`, adjusting `index` by -1 (previous) or +1 (next) accordingly; drop the separate `in` scan in all four functions.
- **L597** `[perf]` _(med)_ — Per-timestep `regridded_snapshot` does an O(N) linear `in` membership scan of the sorted `available_dates` on every call, including cache hits. **Fix:** Use an O(log N) membership test on the sorted array, e.g. `idx = searchsortedfirst(available_dates, date); (idx <= length(available_dates) && available_dates[idx] == date) || error(...)`, and/or move the availability check inside the `get!` closure so cache hits skip it entirely.
- **L557** `[doc-error]` — `next_date`'s docstring says it returns the date itself for a snapshot, but the code returns the following snapshot, contradicting itself and diverging from the `next_time` sibling. **Fix:** Change L557 to 'If `date` is one of the snapshots, return the next date.' (mirroring `next_time`) and fix the signature name in L554 to `date`.
- **L656** `[doc-error]` _(med)_ — regridded_snapshot! docstring signature names/types the third argument as `date::Dates.DateTime`, but the real method parameter is `time` (untyped) and the docstring body itself refers to `time`. **Fix:** Change the header third argument to match the real parameter, e.g. `regridded_snapshot!(dest, data_handler, time)` (or document both `time::AbstractFloat` and `date::Dates.DateTime` overloads), and keep `dest` untyped to match the definition.
- **L253** `[grammar]` — Ungrammatical comment 'the case with have 1 FileReader'. **Fix:** Reword, e.g. '# We have to deal with the case where we have 1 FileReader (with possibly multiple files),'.
- **L263** `[grammar]` _(med)_ — Comment jams the boolean variable name into the sentence, making it read incorrectly ('If is_file_paths_list_of_lists not already a list of lists'). **Fix:** Reword to '# If file_paths is not already a list of lists, we have two options:'.
- **L427** `[grammar]` — Incorrect article 'a' before 'equispaced' in the dt docstring. **Fix:** Change to 'on an equispaced temporal mesh.'
- **L348** `[style]` — The 'additional validation' loop's condition is tautologically false, so its error branch is dead code that can never detect the mismatch it claims to guard against. **Fix:** Delete the dead L344-354 validation loop (and the redundant L342 assert), or replace it with a check that genuinely cross-references ordering; as written it provides no protection.

#### `ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl`

#### `ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl`
- **L205** `[bug]` — Dataset lifecycle reference-counts by a Set of varnames, not by reader count, so two readers sharing the same file AND varname cause a premature close (use-after-close) or a KeyError on close. **Fix:** Reference-count by the number of live readers, not by distinct varnames: store a per-reader count (e.g. an Int, or a Dict{String,Int} / Accumulator keyed by varname) in the OPEN_NCFILES value and only NCDatasets.close + delete! when the total reader count reaches zero. Alternatively track distinct reader object identities. Also guard the pop! (L205) so a varname already removed does not throw.
- **L249** `[perf]` _(med)_ — Dated read does an O(N) linear scan with findall (which also heap-allocates a Vector) to locate a date, even though available_dates is guaranteed sorted, so O(log N) searchsorted applies. **Fix:** Use `idx = searchsortedfirst(file_reader.available_dates, date); (idx <= length(file_reader.available_dates) && file_reader.available_dates[idx] == date) || error("Problem with date $date ...")` and use `idx` directly (no allocation, O(log N)). If strict duplicate detection is still wanted, additionally compare `searchsortedlast`.
- **L254** `[perf]` _(med)_ — The `var = file_reader.dataset[file_reader.varname]` local is used only for its dimnames and then discarded; the same dataset indexing is repeated at line 260, doubling the CFVariable lookup/wrapper construction per read. **Fix:** Reuse the existing binding: `return file_reader.preprocess_func.(var[slicer...])`.
- **L75** `[doc-error]` — Docstring signature type annotation uses a single colon instead of the double-colon required by the real method. **Fix:** Change `cache_max_size:Int = 128,` to `cache_max_size::Int = 128,`.
- **L48** `[typo]` — Misspelling 'physcial' in the dim_names field docstring. **Fix:** Change 'physcial' to 'physical'.
- **L63** `[typo]` — 'a sentinel data' should be 'a sentinel date' in the _cached_reads field docstring. **Fix:** Change 'a sentinel data `DateTime(0)`' to 'a sentinel date `DateTime(0)`'.
- **L95** `[typo]` — Misspelling 'standarizing' in the file_paths normalization comment. **Fix:** Change 'standarizing' to 'standardizing'.
- **L126** `[grammar]` — Comment 'When we have only no time data' is ungrammatical and misdescribes the actual condition (single-file case). **Fix:** Reword to e.g. 'When we have a single file (no time aggregation), we pass a plain string rather than a vector.'

#### `ext/TimeVaryingInputs0DExt.jl`
- **L119** `[bug]` _(med)_ — The ITime epoch-mismatch guard is unreachable, so differing-epoch inputs never hit its clear error and instead crash with a generic message from `promote`. **Fix:** Restructure so the epoch check runs before/independently of the promote branch, e.g. first validate `eltype(times) <: ITime{<:Any,<:Any,Nothing} || all(d -> d.epoch == first(times).epoch, times) || error("...differing epochs")`, and only then promote to unify periods; remove the unreachable `elseif` body.
- **L161** `[bug]` _(med)_ — `_time_range_target_time_dt` indexes `times[begin+1]` with no length guard, so a single-sample PeriodicCalendar input crashes at the first evaluate. **Fix:** Guard early with a clear message, e.g. require `length(times) >= 2` (or `>= 1`) in the constructor, and for the PeriodicCalendar single-sample case emit an explicit error rather than an out-of-range index.
- **L31** `[doc-error]` _(med)_ — Struct docstring refers to a code identifier `values` that does not exist; the field and constructor argument are named `vals`. **Fix:** Replace `values` with `vals` in the docstring so it matches the actual field/argument name.

#### `ext/TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl`
- **L366** `[bug]` — 23D NearestNeighbor evaluation crashes when the requested time equals the last available date, because next_date errors; the exact-date guard present in the LinearInterpolation sibling (and handled by searchsortednearest in the 0D sibling) is missing here. **Fix:** Add the same exact-date guard used by LinearInterpolation before computing the neighbors, e.g. at the top of the non-periodic block: `if time in DataHandling.available_dates(itp.data_handler); regridded_snapshot!(dest, itp.data_handler, time); return nothing; end`. (Equivalently, clamp next_date's index to the last available index.)
- **L277** `[perf]` — PeriodicCalendar (with period) recomputes constant bounding dates via an allocating O(N) filter on every evaluate!. **Fix:** Compute date_init/date_end/dt/dt_e once at construction (store them in the InterpolatingTimeVaryingInput23D struct or a cached field) and read them in _time_range_dt_dt_e instead of recomputing bounding_dates/dt on every evaluate!.
- **L105** `[doc-error]` — Field docstring claims `range` is used by `in()`, but `in()` never reads `range` — it uses `data_handler.available_dates`. **Fix:** Correct the field doc: the `in()` function checks `data_handler.available_dates`, not `range`. Either drop the "Used by the in() function." sentence or update it to reflect that `range` is currently unused by `in`.
- **L281** `[doc-error]` _(med)_ — Worked example gives dt_e = 17 days, but the actual computed dt_e (with the +1 Second) is 18 days. **Fix:** Change the example to `dt_e = 18 days`.
- **L307** `[doc-error]` _(med)_ — Docstring states `t_init`/`t_end` are "in units of simulation time", but the implementation binds them to DateTime dates. **Fix:** Update the docstring to say `t_init`/`t_end` are dates (DateTimes) and `dt`/`dt_e` are `Dates` periods, or otherwise reconcile the "units of simulation time" framing with the date-based implementation.

#### `test/regridders.jl`
- **L265** `[bug]` _(med)_ — Periodic non-end-point error check uses minimum() instead of maximum(), so it passes if any single point matches even when every other point is wrong. **Fix:** Use `maximum(abs.(view(diff_coordinates, inds_not_ends))) ≈ 0.0` (or `all(≈(0.0), abs.(view(diff_coordinates, inds_not_ends)))`) to require every non-end point to have ~0 error.
- **L444** `[bug]` — The dimension-reversal equivalence assertion `result_wrong == result` is trivially true because the input data is all zeros, so it cannot detect a broken reversal. **Fix:** Fill `data_3D` with a non-symmetric field that varies along the reversed dimension (e.g. `data_3D[i,:,:] .= lon[i]`) before regridding, so `result_wrong == result` actually exercises the dimension/data reversal.

#### `test/space_varying_inputs.jl`
- **L61** `[bug]` — Masking/tautological assertion: `field_of_structs.b == 2 .* field_of_structs.a` can never fail, so it never verifies that b was interpolated correctly. **Fix:** Assert `b` against an independent expected value instead of against a derived quantity, e.g. `@test parent(field_of_structs.b)[:] ≈ AT(collect(range(FT(0.2), FT(3.8), 10)))` (2x the expected `a` values), which exercises both the interpolation and the constructor's `b = 2a` derivation.
