#### `src/ITime.jl`
- **L246** `[bug/numerical / overflow (silent wraparound); sibling asymmetry with date()]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — promote() scales the coarser operand's counter by the period ratio with unchecked Int multiplication, silently overflowing on every arithmetic/comparison op that mixes a coarse period with a fine common period. **Fix:** Guard the scaling like date() does, e.g. use `Base.Checked.checked_mul` (throwing on overflow) or widen via `widemul(counter(t), div(period(t), common_period))` and check it fits the counter type before narrowing, mirroring the overflow message in date().
- **L237** `[perf/invariant]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — Every ITime binary op (+, -, <=, >=, ==, isless, isapprox, div, //) calls promote(), which re-derives the common epoch and common period (gcd + epoch reduction) and reconstructs both ITimes, even when both operands already share period and epoch — the universal case in a fixed-period simulation loop. **Fix:** Add a fast path that skips promote when periods and epochs already match (e.g. in the binary-op macros or in promote: `t1.period === t2.period && t1.epoch === t2.epoch` -> operate directly on counters), reserving the full promote for genuinely mixed period/epoch operands. NOTE: whether the filtered…
- **L238** `[perf/invariant]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — promote() has no fast path for operands that already share period and epoch (the norm in a timestep loop), so it recomputes the epoch fold + gcd and rebuilds both operands on every ITime op. **Fix:** Add an early return when the operands are already compatible, e.g. at the top of the 2-arg path: `period(t1) == period(t2) && epoch(t1) == epoch(t2) && return (t1, t2)`. This skips the epoch fold, the gcd, and both struct rebuilds for the common case and lets the op inline down to a bare counter…
- **L261** `[perf/type-instability]` _(impact: medium, effort: moderate)_ — find_common_epoch returns Union{Nothing,DateTime}, making promote() (and therefore every ITime + / - / comparison result) type-unstable in its EPOCH parameter on the per-step hot path. **Fix:** Make the common-epoch result concretely typed. Add type-dispatched 2-arg methods so each branch returns one concrete type, e.g. `find_common_epoch(::ITime{<:Any,<:Any,Nothing}, ::ITime{<:Any,<:Any,Nothing}) = nothing`; `find_common_epoch(a::ITime{<:Any,<:Any,DateTime},…
- **L445** `[perf/dispatch]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — The `@itime_binary_op_notype` comparison ops run the full promote (epoch reduction + gcd + a `map` that constructs two brand-new ITime objects) only to read `.counter` off each and compare integers; the epoch value and the two ITime constructions are pure wasted work on the hottest ITime path. **Fix:** Add a lightweight helper, e.g. `_common_counters(t1,t2)` that validates the epochs are compatible, computes the common period, and returns just the two scaled Integer counters (no ITime construction, no epoch-value reduction), and have `@itime_binary_op_notype` call it instead of `promote`.

#### `src/OnlineLogging.jl`
- **L46** `[bug/error-handling / missing validation (sentinel contamination)]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The -1.0 sentinels for t_wall_last/t_simulation_last are only safe because the default first_update_after_n_calls=2 skips the first two calls, but the constructor never validates this; first_update_after_n_calls < 2 records the sentinels as real data, injecting ~1.75e9 s of bogus wall time plus a negative compensation into ∑Δt_wall. **Fix:** Validate `first_update_after_n_calls >= 2` in the constructor (throw/clamp with a message), or use `nothing`/`missing` sentinels and skip any measurement until t_wall_last and t_simulation_last hold real values.
- **L95** `[bug/numerical / edge-input (division by zero permanently corrupts state)]` _(impact: medium, effort: easy)_ — The first-recorded-measurement compensation divides by simulation_time_since_last = t - t_simulation_last[] with no zero guard; if two callback invocations land at the same simulation time, this is 0 and ∑Δt_wall[] becomes Inf/NaN permanently, poisoning every later average and crashing all subsequent report_walltime calls. **Fix:** Skip compensation when the window is degenerate: `if simulation_time_since_last > 0 ... end` (leave Δt_wall unadjusted otherwise), or derive the rate from Δt_wall / n_steps_this_measurement which already handles the step count.
- **L191** `[bug/numerical / edge-input (division by zero, NaN, crash)]` _(impact: medium, effort: easy)_ — report_walltime divides by n_steps (and by ∑Δt_wall) with no zero guard; called at t <= t_start it computes 0/0 = NaN, and _time_and_units_str(NaN) then throws InexactError converting NaN to Int64. **Fix:** Guard the denominators, e.g. `n_steps <= 0 && return nothing` (or n_steps = max(n_steps,1)) and short-circuit when wt.∑Δt_wall[] == 0.0; additionally harden _time_and_units_str to return a placeholder when its argument is non-finite.
- **L228** `[bug/numerical / integer overflow (Int64), crash]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — _time_and_units_str converts ceil(1e9*seconds) into Dates.Nanosecond (Int64); for seconds greater than ~9.2e9 (~292 yr) this exceeds typemax(Int64) and throws InexactError - hitting exactly the large/early 'unreliable' estimates the docstring warns about. Distinct root from the L227 isapprox item. **Fix:** In _time_and_units_str guard non-finite and out-of-range inputs before nanosecond conversion, e.g. `isfinite(seconds) || return "unknown"; seconds > 9.0e9 && return ">292 years"`, or build the CompoundPeriod from whole Seconds for large durations instead of Nanoseconds.

#### `src/OutputPathGenerator.jl`
- **L158** `[bug/concurrency / MPI collective correctness]` _(impact: medium, effort: moderate)_ — RemovePreexistingStyle has no error_message/bcast safety net at all: if root's rm (158) or mkpath (160) throws, root skips the collective barrier inside maybe_wait_filesystem and the non-root ranks deadlock there forever. **Fix:** Adopt the same error_message + bcast pattern used by ActiveLinkStyle: wrap the root rm/mkpath in try/catch storing an error_message, `error_message = bcast(context, error_message)`, and error on all ranks — guaranteeing every rank reaches maybe_wait_filesystem's barrier.
- **L160** `[bug/mpi]` _(impact: medium, effort: moderate)_ — RemovePreexistingStyle deadlocks non-root ranks if root's rm/mkpath throws: root skips the barrier inside maybe_wait_filesystem while non-root ranks wait there. **Fix:** Mirror the ActiveLinkStyle design: run the root-only rm/mkpath inside try/catch, capture any failure into an error_message, bcast it to all ranks after (or before) the barrier, and have every rank `error(error_message)` together so a failure aborts cleanly on all ranks instead of hanging.
- **L215** `[bug/mpi]` _(impact: medium, effort: moderate)_ — ActiveLinkStyle root-only filesystem ops (rm old link L215, mkpath L197/L247) are outside the error_message mechanism, so a failure throws on root only and deadlocks non-root ranks at the following bcast. **Fix:** Bring every root-only filesystem operation in the L188-271 block under the error_message mechanism: wrap them (individually or the whole block) in try/catch that sets error_message on failure, so any failure is broadcast at L272 and raised on all ranks instead of thrown only on root.
- **L350** `[bug/edge inputs / error handling]` _(impact: medium, effort: easy)_ — detect_restart_file crashes with an uncaught SystemError when a non-directory entry matches the output_XXXX pattern, instead of returning nothing as documented. **Fix:** Filter to directories only, e.g. `filter(x -> isdir(joinpath(base_output_dir, x)) && !isnothing(match(name_rx, x)), readdir(base_output_dir))`, or guard the per-folder readdir with `isdir(previous_folder) || continue`.
- **L347** `[doc-error/correctness / docstring-vs-code semantics]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — detect_restart_file applies sort_func only WITHIN the first (highest-numbered) output folder that contains any match, but the docstring promises the most recent restart file across the whole directory structure — so a custom simulation-time sort_func can return the wrong file. **Fix:** Either (a) collect all matching files across all folders (as full paths) and apply sort_func once over the whole set, taking `last`, to honor the documented cross-structure 'most recent' contract; or (b) narrow the docstring to state that selection is by output-folder number first and sort_func…

#### `src/Regridders.jl`
- **L63** `[bug/API consistency / sibling asymmetry]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — `regrid!` is a public entry point (defined line 26, implemented in InterpolationsRegridderExt) but is missing from `extension_fns`, so a `regrid!` MethodError gets no "Import X" hint while its sibling `regrid` does. **Fix:** Add `:regrid!` alongside `:regrid` in the `:ClimaCore` and `:Interpolations` entries (regrid! is only implemented by InterpolationsRegridder), e.g. `:ClimaCore => [:InterpolationsRegridder, :regrid, :regrid!]` and the same for `:Interpolations`.
- **L55** `[style/error handling / actionable messages]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — `error("No regridder available")` in default_regridder_type gives no guidance on how to fix it, bypassing the whole "Import X" hint machinery this module invests in elsewhere. **Fix:** Make the message actionable, e.g. `error("No regridder available. Import ClimaCore and Interpolations (for InterpolationsRegridder) or ClimaCoreTempestRemap (for TempestRegridder).")`.

#### `src/SpaceVaryingInputs.jl`
- **L11** `[doc-error/docstring-vs-code semantics]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The header comment calls the four array kinds 'planned' even though all four are implemented in the extension, so it reads as unfinished/future work when it is not. **Fix:** Replace 'The planned parameter underlying arrays are' with 'The supported parameter underlying arrays are' (or 'This module supports').

#### `src/TimeManager.jl`
- **L77** `[bug/API consistency & sibling-asymmetry / incomplete implementation]` _(impact: medium, effort: easy)_ — EveryTimestep is exported and documented as a dispatch type for trigger_callback, but no trigger_callback method accepts it (only ::Monthly exists), so every use of the advertised every-timestep frequency throws MethodError. **Fix:** Add a method for the exported type, e.g. `function trigger_callback(date_nextcall, date_current, ::EveryTimestep, func::Function, func_args::Tuple); func(func_args...); return date_nextcall; end` (and/or an `::AbstractFrequency` fallback) mirroring the Monthly method.
- **L108** `[bug/correctness / calendar arithmetic (latent)]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — trigger_callback advances the next-call date with `+ Dates.Month(1)`, which for end-of-month anchor dates permanently drifts to an earlier day-of-month, so 'monthly' callbacks anchored late in the month fire on shifting/earlier days. **Fix:** If month-end/day-preserving semantics are intended, track the intended day-of-month (or anchor on firstdayofmonth) and recompute against the target month's lastdayofmonth instead of repeatedly adding Month(1) to a drifting date; otherwise document the drift explicitly.
- **L52** `[doc-error/docstring-vs-code semantics]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — strdate_to_datetime's docstring says it converts 'to Date format', but the function returns a Dates.DateTime, not a Dates.Date. **Fix:** Change 'to Date format' to 'to a `DateTime`' (or, if a `Date` is genuinely intended, return `Dates.Date(...)` and rename accordingly, which would change behavior).

#### `src/TimeVaryingInputs.jl`
- **L305** `[perf/type stability / sibling API asymmetry]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation.period` is declared with the abstract type `DatePeriod`, making field access type-unstable, unlike every sibling method which parametrizes its fields. **Fix:** Add a type parameter mirroring PeriodicCalendar: `struct LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation{P<:DatePeriod, BC<:AbstractInterpolationBoundaryMethod} <: AbstractInterpolationMethod; period::P; extrapolation_bc::BC; ... end`.
- **L93** `[doc-error/docstring rendering semantics]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — `!!! warn` is not a recognized Documenter admonition category; it should be `!!! warning`, otherwise the box renders with an incorrect/custom title rather than as a warning. **Fix:** Change `!!! warn` to `!!! warning`.
- **L115** `[doc-error/incorrect docstring semantics (type vs instance)]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The PeriodicCalendar docstring says the equivalent first-mode call uses `period = Dates.Year` (the type) instead of an instance `Dates.Year(1)`, and omits the required repeat_date. **Fix:** Write `period = Dates.Year(1)` and note that a `repeat_date` must also be supplied in first mode.
- **L175** `[doc-error/docstring-vs-code semantics (runnable example)]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The TimeVaryingInput docstring example defines `CO2fromp` but then constructs the input from an undefined `CO2fromY`, so the example errors if copied. **Fix:** Use one consistent name: either define `CO2fromp` and call `TimeVaryingInput(CO2fromp)`, or rename the definition to `CO2fromY`.

### EXT (Pass 6)

#### `ext/DataHandlingExt.jl`
- **L282** `[bug/resource management / error handling]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — NCFileReaders opened during construction are leaked (never closed) if a later reader fails to open or if any of the post-construction consistency @asserts throw, because each reader registers its dataset in the process-global OPEN_NCFILES and the partially-built DataHandler is never returned. **Fix:** Wrap reader construction and the consistency checks in a try/catch that closes any already-opened readers before rethrowing (e.g. `try ... catch; foreach(close, values(file_readers)); rethrow(); end`), and give the three @asserts explicit, actionable messages.

For a fixed DataHandler the target_space+regridder produce a single homogeneous concrete Field type, so derive it once (from one regrid, or from the target space + FT) and build `LRUCache{DateTime, typeof(field)}`; relax the struct bound at…
- **L666** `[perf/fusion]` _(impact: medium, effort: large)_ — regridded_snapshot! always does a full grid-sized copy of the (already-materialized, usually cached) Field into dest, which on the LinearInterpolation path costs two redundant grid-sized copy kernels per timestep. **Fix:** Expose/rely on the ref-returning path for read-only interpolation: have the LinearInterpolation caller do `f0 = regridded_snapshot(dh, date0); f1 = regridded_snapshot(dh, date1); dest .= (1-coeff).*f0 .+ coeff.*f1`, dropping field_t0/field_t1 and the two copy kernels (safe because cache_max_size>=2…

#### `ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl`

(e.g. verify `N == length(totuple(first_coord))`/coordinate arity) that raises a clear 'regrid! does not support dimension reduction; use…
- **L191** `[perf/memory-layout]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — In the Z-only-space-with-3D-data branch, the center-column extraction slices with a large stride (dims 2/3) and allocates a fresh Vector without @view, hurting locality. **Fix:** Use `@view` for the column extraction where the downstream interpolant accepts a SubArray (`data = @view data[h1_idx, :, h2_idx]`), and prefer the contiguous z-as-dim-1 orientation when the data layout is under your control; the allocation/stride cost is otherwise repeated every regrid.

- **L197** `[perf/logging / concurrency (MPI)]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The dim_names-missing warning in regrid fires with no `maxlog`, so it is re-emitted on every regrid (i.e. every cache-miss / new time sample) and independently on every MPI rank, producing hot-path log spam. **Fix:** Add `maxlog=1` to the `@warn` (`@warn "..." maxlog=1`) so the assumption is reported once per process, and/or gate it to the root rank via `ClimaComms` when a context is available.

- **L151** `[style/API consistency / maintainability]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The 'what counts as a time dimension' predicate is duplicated verbatim in two places in this file (L107-108 and L150-151) and a third canonical list lives in nc_common.jl's read_available_dates, creating three definitions that can silently diverge. **Fix:** Factor the alias set / predicate into a single shared constant or helper (e.g. a const TIME_DIM_NAMES tuple plus one is_time function reused in both nc_common.jl and NCFileReaderExt.jl) and reference it from all three sites.

- **L19** `[bug/error handling / robustness]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — read_available_dates decides which time axis to read by inspecting dimension names (ds.dim) but then reads the same-named variable; a time dimension that lacks a coordinate variable throws a raw KeyError instead of falling through to the next candidate or returning empty. **Fix:** Guard on the variable existing, not just the dimension, e.g. iterate over candidates checking `haskey(ds, name)` (or `name in keys(ds)`), and only then read; fall through to `date`/empty otherwise, raising a descriptive error if no usable coordinate is found.

#### `ext/time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl`
- **L204** `[perf/type-stability/dispatch]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation.period is declared with the ABSTRACT type DatePeriod, so method.period is read as an abstractly-typed value every evaluate! step, defeating compile-time specialization of the period-arithmetic helpers and forcing dynamic dispatch on `DateTime + period`. **Fix:** Parametrize the struct on the period type: `struct LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation{P<:DatePeriod, BC<:AbstractInterpolationBoundaryMethod}; period::P; extrapolation_bc::BC end` and construct with `new{typeof(period), typeof(bc)}(period, bc)`. Then `method.period` is a concrete Year(1), the…
- **L290** `[perf/fusion]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The standalone in-place scaling `dest .*= (1 - coeff)` (L290 interpolable branch, L363 else branch) is an extra grid-sized broadcast kernel that can be folded into the final combine, giving one fused kernel instead of two/three. **Fix:** Drop L290 and L297 and replace L298 with a single fused kernel after both evaluate! calls: `@. dest = (1 - coeff) * dest + coeff * tmp_field1`. Do the same in the else branch: remove L363 and L365, replace L366 with `@. dest = (1 - coeff) * dest + coeff * tmp_field2` (keep `coeff` computed at L362…
- **L311** `[perf/redundant-computation]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — _move_date_to_period(target_date, period_left, period) is computed at line 261 and then recomputed identically at line 275 (interpolable branch) and line 311 (else branch), redundantly re-running the period arithmetic each step. **Fix:** Reuse the line-261 value: in the interpolable branch set `date_pre = target_date_in_left_period` (drop the recompute at line 275), and in the else branch delete the recompute at line 311 (target_date_in_left_period is already in scope), keeping only the new `target_date_in_right_period` at line 313.
- **L318** `[perf/algorithmic]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — `minimum(...)`/`maximum(...)` are called on the sorted per-period date subsets (L318, L319, L337, L338 in the else branch and L184, L188 inside `_interpolable_range`), each an O(N_period) scan where `first(...)`/`last(...)` is O(1); several also duplicate reductions `_interpolable_range` already performed. **Fix:** Replace `minimum(dates_period_left)`->`first(dates_period_left)`, `maximum(dates_period_left)`->`last(dates_period_left)`, and likewise for `dates_period_right` (and `dates_period_right_moved_to_left`, whose first/last equal `first/last(dates_period_right) - period_offset`). Better: have…
- **L59** `[doc-error/docstring-vs-code semantics]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The `_neighboring_periods` docstring passes `date` as a 1-element Vector (the function/call site use a scalar) and includes a stray `_extract_period` doctest copy-pasted from another function. **Fix:** Change the example to pass a scalar `DateTime(1993, 8, 18)` and delete the stray `_extract_period` doctest at lines 62-63.
- **L145** `[doc-error/docstring-vs-code semantics]` _(impact: low, effort: easy)_ — The `_interpolable_range` docstring shows the return value as a Vector and gives example outputs the code cannot produce, including one that would throw instead of returning. **Fix:** Rewrite the examples to show a tuple `(DateTime(1985,1,15), DateTime(1985,12,11))`, correct the 148 result to `1985-01-15`, and make the 150-151 right-period input use dates all within one period so it does not hit the different-periods error.

### OTHER (Pass 6)

#### `/home/kphan/Desktop/work_tree/mainRepos/ClimaUtilities.jl/find-bugs/ext/nc_common.jl`
- **L22** `[bug/API consistency / sibling-asymmetry]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — 'date' is interpreted here as integer yyyymmdd, but NCFileReaderExt treats 'date' as an interchangeable CF time dimension for aggregation/indexing; a CF-encoded 'date' axis is aggregated fine yet crashes read_available_dates. **Fix:** Detect the encoding (CFTime element type vs integer) rather than keying off the name 'date': if the variable's eltype is a CFTime/date-time type use the reinterpret path, else parse yyyymmdd.
- **L23** `[bug/edge inputs / robustness]` _(impact: low, effort: moderate)_ — The 'date' branch assumes values are integers in exactly yyyymmdd form; float-encoded or non-8-digit dates silently misparse or throw. **Fix:** Convert to Int before stringifying (e.g. `string.(Int.(ds["date"][:]))`) and/or zero-pad to 8 digits (lpad) as datetime_to_strdate does, and validate the digit count before parsing.

## Pass 7 — dedicated performance re-sweep (novel-lens, verified)

> **Status / provenance.** A focused performance-only re-sweep: **9 dimension/file-specialized finders** over every hot-path file (`ext/DataHandlingExt.jl`, `ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl`+`nc_common.jl`, `ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl`, `ext/TempestRegridderExt.jl`+`SpaceVaryingInputsExt.jl`, `ext/TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl`, `ext/TimeVaryingInputs0DExt.jl`+`time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl`, `src/Utils.jl`+`DataStructures.jl`, `src/ITime.jl`), plus a cross-cutting lens (boxed closures, non-const globals, `invokelatest`/dynamic dispatch, eager error-string interpolation, un-fused/temp-allocating broadcasts, materialize-vs-view). Each finder was given the **exact known-perf lines from Passes 1–6 for its files** and told to report only genuinely new locations. Every candidate was then **adversarially verified** against source (is it truly hot? is the cost real and the fix sound? is it a duplicate?). **13 candidates → 5 CONFIRMED new, 5 duplicates, 3 rejected.** No Julia executed (static-only, per standing instruction). All line numbers re-checked against the current source.
>
> **Honest impact note:** the six prior passes had already caught every high-impact perf issue; all 5 new Pass-7 findings are **low / negligible** micro-optimizations (small scalar/coordinate-sized allocations or O(N)→O(log N) on small N, dwarfed by the grid-sized regrid/broadcast work on the same call). They are genuinely avoidable and correct to fix, but none is a hot-loop bottleneck.

| Location | perf (new) |
|---|---|
| EXT | 5 |
| **Total** | **5** |

### EXT (Pass 7)

#### `ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl`
- **L320** `[perf]` _(impact: low)_ — In the in-place `Regridders.regrid!(output, regridder::InterpolationsRegridder, data, dimensions)`, the periodic-longitude (`lon_oncell`) branch does `dimensions = deepcopy(dimensions)` (L320) and then mutates only the longitude vector via `push!(lon, last(lon) + dlon)` (L321-323). Deep-copying the whole `NTuple` of coordinate vectors is doubly wasteful: (1) the untouched lat/z/other axis vectors are copied for no reason (they are only read and passed unchanged to `Intp.interpolate`, which does not mutate its knot vectors), and (2) `deepcopy` is much heavier than a plain `copy` — it recursively traverses the structure and allocates an internal `IdDict` for cycle detection on every call. **Why hot:** `regrid!` is the public in-place regrid entry point; on global equispaced 360°-periodic-longitude data (the common global-forcing layout) the `lon_oncell` branch fires on every `regrid!` call. (Note: the package's own per-time-sample path uses the allocating `regrid`, not `regrid!`, so this line is only hit by downstream in-place callers.) **Distinct from** the documented `regrid`-side findings (L163/L210/L245/L255/L276), which all live in the *allocating* `regrid` (L152-267); none touch the `deepcopy` at L320 in `regrid!`. **Fix:** Copy only the longitude vector and rebuild the tuple sharing the other vectors: `lon = copy(dimensions[lon_dim_idx]); push!(lon, last(lon) + (lon[2] - lon[1])); dimensions = Base.setindex(dimensions, lon, lon_dim_idx)` — behavior-preserving and type-stable (all elements are the same concrete `Vector{FT}`). **Impact:** low — coordinate vectors are 1-D (KB-scale), dwarfed by the grid-sized `cat` in `_append_first_slice` (L319) and the target-space broadcast (L335) in the same call, but the allocation is genuine and avoidable.

#### `ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl`
- **L236** `[perf]` _(impact: negligible)_ — In `FileReaders.read(file_reader::NCFileReader, date::Dates.DateTime)`, the common cache-hit path probes the LRU cache's underlying `Dict` twice for the same key: `haskey(file_reader._cached_reads, date)` (L236) hashes+probes the DateTime key, then `file_reader._cached_reads[date]` (L237) hashes+probes it a second time (before the `copy` and the O(N) `_update_priority!`). A single traversal suffices. **Why hot:** `read` runs per read; this hit branch is exercised whenever the raw snapshot for `date` is still cached (e.g. `LinearInterpolation` re-reading `date0`/`date1` whose regridded field was evicted from the size-2 regrid cache but whose raw slice survives in the size-128 read cache). **Distinct from** the documented L237 finding (which is about type instability from the abstract `Array` element type — a different mechanism). **Fix:** Do one lookup, e.g. `cached = Base.get(file_reader._cached_reads.cache, date, nothing); if cached !== nothing; DataStructures._update_priority!(file_reader._cached_reads, date); return copy(cached); end` (Array values are never `nothing`, so the sentinel is safe), or add an LRUCache accessor that fetches and bumps recency in one probe. **Impact:** negligible — one `Int64`-keyed `Dict` probe, dwarfed on the same line by the full-array `copy()` and the always-present O(N) `_update_priority!` `filter!`, and downstream by the accompanying regrid.

#### `ext/time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl`
- **L159** `[perf]` _(impact: low)_ — In `_interpolable_range(dates_period_left, dates_period_right, period)`, the two sanity checks `length(unique(beginningofperiod.(dates_period_left, period))) != 1` (L159) and its twin for `dates_period_right` (L162) each materialize a broadcast result `Vector` **plus** a `unique` result (Set + Vector) purely to test that all dates share one period (cardinality == 1). This validation runs on the success path. **Why hot:** `_interpolable_range` is called at L266 inside the LinearPeriodFilling `evaluate!` kernel on the gap-filling path (target date not in an available period), i.e. per timestep during gap filling. **Distinct** allocation site — not among the documented lines for this file (L68/L172/L183/L187/L204/L211/L240/L247/L253/L290/L297/L311/L318/L319/L337/L338/L361). **Fix:** Replace each `length(unique(beginningofperiod.(xs, period))) != 1` with an allocation-free scan, e.g. `p0 = beginningofperiod(first(xs), period); any(d -> beginningofperiod(d, period) != p0, xs)` (lazy generator, no array; the vectors are non-empty on this path). **Impact:** low — the vectors hold the dates within a single period (small, e.g. ~12 monthly entries), so the few tiny allocations per gap-fill step are minor next to the regrid/interpolation work, but genuinely avoidable.
- **L218** `[perf]` _(impact: negligible)_ — In `evaluate!(dest, itp::InterpolatingTimeVaryingInput23D, time, ::LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation)`, the fast-path guard `_extract_period(target_date, period) in available_periods` (L218) is an O(N) linear membership scan, even though `available_periods` (L211 = `unique_periods(...)`) is produced sorted ascending (`Utils.jl:389` ends `|> sort`). **Why hot:** top-of-`evaluate!` guard, run per timestep (and again via the recursive `evaluate!` at L361). **Distinct from** the documented L68 (`findfirst` in `_neighboring_periods`) and L211 (`unique_periods` recompute) — this is the `in` membership test, a separate line/mechanism. **Fix:** `insorted(_extract_period(target_date, period), available_periods)` — same Bool on a sorted vector, type-stable, non-allocating. **Impact:** negligible — `in` does not allocate, N (unique periods) is small (tens), and this O(N)→O(log N) win is dwarfed by the L211 `map|>unique|>sort` recompute on the same data every call (fix them together).
- **L275** `[perf]` _(impact: negligible)_ — In the `in_interpolable_region` branch of the same `evaluate!`, `date_pre = _move_date_to_period(target_date, period_left, period)` (L275) recomputes byte-for-byte the value already bound at L261-262 as `target_date_in_left_period` (identical arguments). `_move_date_to_period` does two `beginningofperiod` calls plus period subtraction/addition — all redundant here. **Why hot:** runs per timestep whenever the target lands in the interpolable region of a LinearPeriodFilling input. **Distinct from** the documented L311 recompute, which is the same pattern in the *else* branch (a physically separate line; fixing one does not fix the other). **Fix:** Reuse the existing binding: `date_pre = target_date_in_left_period`. **Impact:** negligible — a scalar date computation dwarfed by the two full-field regrid `evaluate!` calls and whole-field broadcasts in the same branch.

## Pass 8 — novel-lens performance re-sweep (verified)

> **Status / provenance.** A second performance-only re-sweep aimed at angles the seven prior passes never specifically hunted: **5 novel-lens finders** — (1) **GPU / device-array scalar-indexing hazards** on ClimaCore Fields (scalar `getindex`/`setindex`/reduction that forces `allowscalar` fallback or host↔device transfer per step); (2) **whole-call-chain compound / architectural** tracing of the 23D & 0D `evaluate!` chains end-to-end (gains not attributable to a single line); (3) **kwargs/args-splat & abstract positional-arg dispatch** de-specialization in the `evaluate!`/`regrid`/`read` overloads; (4) **ITime per-op costs beyond `promote`** (op macros, `date()`, `float`/`seconds` conversions, `Base.:*(::Float,::ITime)`); (5) **never-perf-audited hot-ish code** (`OnlineLogging._update!`, `TimeManager.trigger_callback`, remaining `LRUCache` accessors, `Utils` period helpers). Each finder got the full Pass 1–7 exclusion list; every candidate was **adversarially verified** against source. **6 candidates → 3 CONFIRMED new, 2 duplicates, 1 rejected.** No Julia executed (static-only).
>
> **Clean-lens results (no new findings — a useful negative):** the **GPU scalar-indexing**, **whole-chain/architectural**, and **dispatch/splat** lenses each returned **nothing new**. The per-step `evaluate!`/`regrid` kernels operate on Fields via whole-array broadcasts (device-friendly, no stray scalar Field indexing on hot paths beyond the already-noted 0D `itp.vals[end]` at `TimeVaryingInputs0DExt.jl:221`, which is a small host Vector anyway); the interpolation call chains have no compound/shared-work gain left un-catalogued by Passes 1–7; and the `evaluate!` overloads are already resolved by multiple dispatch (the abstract-typed costs that remain are the *struct-field* ones already documented, not argument dispatch).
>
> **Honest impact note:** all 3 new Pass-8 findings are **negligible** micro-optimizations (a single scalar integer division; a couple of redundant scalar `float()`/field loads in a low-frequency progress callback). They are correct, no-downside cleanups but have no measurable runtime effect. **Conclusion: after 8 passes the performance surface is exhausted — no remaining medium/high-impact hot-path gains were found.**

| Location | perf (new) |
|---|---|
| SRC | 3 |
| **Total** | **3** |

### SRC (Pass 8)

#### `src/ITime.jl`
- **L154** `[perf]` _(impact: negligible)_ — In `date(t::ITime)`, the overflow guard spends a full scalar integer division per call: after `elapsed_period = counter(t) * period(t)` (L142), line 154 computes `no_overflow = period_is_zero || div(elapsed_period, period(t)) == counter(t)` (plus the `period(t) == zero(period(t))` compare at L153). The `div` merely re-divides the product back out by the period solely to detect that the value-field multiply did not overflow `Int` — an overflow the multiply itself could report. **Why hot:** `date(t::ITime)` runs once per timestep for ITime-typed times — `evaluate!(dest, itp, time::ITime, ...)` forwards to `evaluate!(dest, itp, date(time), ...)` (`TimeVaryingInputsExt.jl:251`, `time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl:398`), and `==(::ITime, ::DateTime)` also calls it. **Distinct from** the documented `ITime.jl:245/246` promote-overflow item (different function `Base.promote`, different mechanism). **Fix:** Detect the multiply overflow directly: `prod, ovf = Base.Checked.mul_with_overflow(counter(t), period(t).value); ovf && error("Overflow ..."); return current_date + typeof(period(t))(prod)`. `mul_with_overflow(c, 0) == (0, false)` preserves the zero-period path (dropping the separate `== zero(...)` check), and the non-overflow result equals `elapsed_period`, so behavior — including the overflow error — is identical while removing the per-call division and comparison. **Impact:** negligible — one scalar integer division per step (not per grid element, not a GPU op), dwarfed by the surrounding interpolation/regrid work; a clean no-downside micro-opt (and marginally *more* correct, since the checked multiply has no modular false-negatives).

#### `src/OnlineLogging.jl`
- **L73** `[perf]` _(impact: negligible)_ — In `_update!(wt, integrator)`, `t_start, _ = float.(integrator.sol.prob.tspan)` (L73) runs a 3-deep field-access chain plus a tuple broadcast on every call, yet `t_start` is consumed only at L91 — inside the doubly-nested `if should_record_measurement` / `if wt.∑Δt_wall[] == 0.0` block that executes at most **once per simulation** (the first recorded measurement). **Why hot:** `_update!` is called by the `report_walltime` progress callback (low-frequency, but repeatedly). **Distinct:** `OnlineLogging.jl` had no prior perf findings. **Fix:** Move `t_start = float(first(integrator.sol.prob.tspan))` inside the `if wt.∑Δt_wall[] == 0.0` branch so the fetch happens only when used. **Impact:** negligible — `tspan` is a stack 2-tuple (no heap alloc), `float` on Float64 is a no-op, and the same call's `@info` log + `Dates.canonicalize`/string formatting dominate by orders of magnitude.
- **L101** `[perf]` _(impact: negligible)_ — In the same `_update!`, `wt.t_simulation_last[] = float(integrator.t)` (L101) recomputes `float(integrator.t)`, a value already bound to the local `t` at L72; `integrator.t` is not mutated anywhere in the call. **Why hot:** every `_update!` call from the progress callback. **Fix:** Reuse the local — `wt.t_simulation_last[] = t`. **Impact:** negligible — a single struct-field load + `float()` that is effectively identity and likely CSE'd by the compiler. (Note: the L89 recompute the finder also flagged is gated inside the once-per-simulation `∑Δt_wall[] == 0.0` branch, so it is *not* a per-step cost.)

## Pass 9 — correctness-bug + simplification sweep (verified)

> **Status / provenance.** A broad **correctness + simplification** re-sweep (a different lens from the eight perf passes): **11 finders** — 9 per-file/file-group with a combined correctness+simplification lens over all `src/` + `ext/` production code, plus a cross-cutting **sibling-asymmetry/copy-paste** specialist and a **dead-code/DRY** specialist. Each finder got the ~138 already-documented bug/style lines for its files to exclude. Every candidate was **adversarially verified** against source (a bug must reproduce via a concrete failure scenario; a simplification must be strictly behavior-preserving; default REJECT). **19 candidates → 15 confirmed by verifiers**, from which I dropped **2 more** as duplicates of existing `[perf]` findings (`src/Utils.jl:40` and `time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl:311` — both already logged with the identical fix; the Pass-9 dedup list only carried bug/style lines, not perf lines, so the verifiers didn't catch the collision) and **merged** within-set duplicates. **Final: 1 new correctness bug + 9 new simplifications.** No Julia executed (static-only).
>
> **Headline:** one genuinely valuable new **medium-severity correctness bug** — `InterpolationsRegridder.regrid` crashes (or silently mis-orients) whenever its dimension-reduction paths fire on data with a decreasing axis. The simplifications are mostly **DRY consolidations** (duplicated method bodies / error-handling blocks / index logic) plus a few dead-code removals; none change behavior.

| Location | bug (new) | simplification (new) |
|---|---|---|
| SRC | 0 | 4 |
| EXT | 1 | 5 |
| **Total** | **1** | **9** |

### ⭐ New correctness bug (Pass 9)

- ⭐ **`ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl:219`** `[bug]` _(severity: medium)_ — In `Regridders.regrid(regridder, data, dimensions)`, the two **dimension-reduction** branches — drop-z (L156-168, LatLongZ coords + non-extruded target + 2D data) and center-column extraction (L170-208, Z-only coords + 3D data) — reduce `data` and `dimensions` but **never reduce/remap `regridder.dim_increasing`**, which keeps its original (larger) length. Two downstream failures result: **(a)** L210 `map(dimensions, regridder.dim_increasing)` silently zips to the shorter tuple, so after the center-column reduction the surviving dimension is `dimensions[z_idx]` but the reversal flag applied is `dim_increasing[1]` — the **wrong flag whenever `z_idx != 1`**, giving silently wrong (non-monotonic-knot) interpolation; **(b)** L216-219 build `decreasing_indices` from the full-length `dim_increasing` and call `reverse(data, dims = decreasing_indices)` on the **already-reduced** `data`, so a `false` flag at an index beyond the reduced array's `ndims` throws `ArgumentError: invalid dimension`. **Failure scenario:** a Z-only-space regridder with `dim_names = ("lon","lat","z")` and `dim_increasing = (true, false, true)` (decreasing latitude — common in NetCDF) called as `regrid(reg, data_3D, (lon, lat, z))`: the center-column branch reduces `data` to 1-D and `dimensions` to `(z,)`, then `!all(dim_increasing)` is true, `decreasing_indices = (2,)`, and `reverse(data_1D, dims = (2,))` throws `ArgumentError: invalid dimension 2 ≠ 1`. The analogous LatLongZ drop-z case with a decreasing 3rd flag hits `reverse(data_2D, dims = (3,))` → `ArgumentError`. The tests only exercise the Z-only 3D path with the default all-increasing `dim_increasing`, so `!all(...)` is never true and the bug is uncaught. **Distinct from** the documented `regrid!` findings at L287/L323 (different function/mechanism). **Fix:** In each reduction branch produce a reduced/remapped `dim_increasing` matching the surviving dimensions — center-column: `dim_increasing_reduced = (regridder.dim_increasing[z_idx],)` (fallback `(regridder.dim_increasing[3],)`); drop-z: `regridder.dim_increasing[1:2]`; else the full tuple — and use `dim_increasing_reduced` at L210 and L216-218 so knot-reversal and data-reversal stay aligned with the reduced arrays.

### Simplifications (Pass 9)

#### `src/ITime.jl`
- **L303** `[style]` _(simplification, low)_ — `Base.:*(a::AbstractFloat, t::ITime)` (L303-311) is a byte-for-byte copy of `Base.:*(t::ITime, a::AbstractFloat)` (L292-300): identical `[0,1]` guard, identical error string, identical `ITime(round(typeof(t.counter), a * t.counter), t.period, t.epoch)` return. The two must be kept in sync by hand. **Fix:** Replace the whole L303-311 body with a one-line delegation `Base.:*(a::AbstractFloat, t::ITime) = t * a` (dispatches to the other method, no recursion; behavior-preserving including the out-of-range error).
- **L474** `[style]` _(simplification, low)_ — `Base.:*(t::T, num::Integer) where {T<:ITime}` (L474-475) is character-identical to `Base.:*(num::Integer, t::T)` (L472-473); both return `ITime(num * t.counter, t.period, t.epoch)`. **Fix:** `Base.:*(t::T, num::Integer) where {T<:ITime} = num * t`.
- **L333** `[style]` _(simplification, low)_ — In `Base.:(:)(start::ITime, step::ITime, stop::ITime)`, after `start, step, stop = promote(start, step, stop)` (L332) all three operands already carry the unified epoch, so `common_epoch = find_common_epoch(start, step, stop)` (L333) folds over now-identical epochs to recompute a value already available as `start.epoch`. **Fix:** `common_epoch = start.epoch` (or use `start.epoch` directly in the generator), dropping the redundant generator+reduce over `_unique_epochs`. Behavior-preserving (post-promote epochs are all equal, or all `nothing`).

#### `ext/DataHandlingExt.jl`
- **L337** `[style]` _(simplification, trivial)_ — In the `:InterpolationsRegridder` constructor branch, `issorted(dim) ? true : false` is a redundant conditional over a value that is already a `Bool`. **Fix:** replace with `issorted(dim)`.
- **L342** `[style]` _(simplification, low)_ — The assertion `@assert length(dim_increasing) == length(dim_names)` is dead: `dim_increasing` is built by `map(dimensions, dim_names) do … end` (L335), so `map` already guarantees the length matches `dim_names`. The assert can never fail for inputs that reach it. **Fix:** delete the L342 assertion.
- **L492** `[style]` _(simplification, medium)_ — The snapshot-index logic is duplicated across four functions: `previous_time` (L492-504) and `previous_date` (L540-551) contain byte-identical `date in available_dates ? searchsortedfirst : searchsortedfirst - 1` + `index < 1` bounds-check blocks, differing only in whether they finally index `available_times` or `available_dates`; likewise `next_time` (L520-530) and `next_date` (L561-570). Since `available_times[i]` corresponds to `available_dates[i]` (L305), the index math is fully shared, so any future fix to the boundary handling must currently be replicated four times (a sibling-asymmetry hazard). **Fix:** extract `_previous_index(data_handler, date)` and `_next_index(data_handler, date)` helpers, then implement `previous_time = available_times[_previous_index(…)]`, `previous_date = available_dates[_previous_index(…)]` (and analogously for next). Behavior-preserving. _(Distinct from the documented `[perf]` L544 finding, which addresses the O(N) `in` scan inside these functions; this addresses the code duplication — fix both together.)_

#### `ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl`
- **L301** `[style]` _(simplification, medium)_ — The `lon_oncell` detection block in `regrid!` (L301-315) is a near-verbatim copy of the one in `regrid` (L226-241): same `isnothing(lon_dim_idx)`/length guard and same `extrapolation_bc == Intp.Periodic() && length(dim) > 1 && span≈360 && isequispaced(dim)` heuristic, differing only in inputs (`regridder.coordinates`/`dimensions` vs `coords`/`dimensions_FT`). Any change to the "centers-of-cells" heuristic must be made twice, risking `regrid`/`regrid!` silently diverging. **Fix:** factor a helper `_lon_is_oncell(lon_dim_idx, dims, extrapolation_bc)` and call it from both entry points. Behavior-preserving.

#### `ext/TempestRegridderExt.jl`
- **L412** `[style]` _(simplification, low)_ — In `hdwrite_regridfile_rll_to_cgll`, the weight-file read materializes three arrays `(Array(ds_wt["S"]), Array(ds_wt["col"]), Array(ds_wt["row"]))` (L413) but immediately discards two via `_, _, row_indices` (L412). Only `row` is used downstream (L421-424); the remap weighting was already applied by `apply_remap` when producing `datafile_cgll`, so reading `S` (the full nonzero-weight vector — potentially large) and `col` is dead I/O + allocation with no effect. **Fix:** read only the needed variable — `row_indices = NCDatasets.NCDataset(weightfile, "r") do ds_wt; Array(ds_wt["row"]); end`. Byte-identical output; this is dead work, not a missing weighted mat-vec.

#### `src/ClimaArtifacts.jl`
- **L139** `[style]` _(simplification, medium)_ — The `try`/`catch` that wraps `Base.invokelatest(JuliaArtifacts._artifact_str, …)::String` and, on an `ErrorException`, appends the "artifact may also be too large…" hint (rebuilding a new `ErrorException` and rethrowing, else rethrowing `e`) is duplicated **verbatim four times** in `@clima_artifact`: L127-147 and L150-170 (constant-name branch) and again in the variable-name branch (~L207-227 and ~L232-252). All four `catch e` blocks and the inline `msg` literal are byte-for-byte identical (~36 lines); the `try` bodies differ only in passing compile-time-interpolated values vs runtime locals. A maintainer editing the hint or the exception-classification in one copy would silently produce inconsistent errors depending on which branch/call raised. **Fix:** add a module-level helper `_artifact_str_hint(mod, toml, name, tail, dict, hash, platform, lazy)` doing the `try`/`invokelatest`/`catch`+rethrow-with-hint once, and emit `ClimaArtifacts._artifact_str_hint(…)` at all four sites (macro hygiene resolves the unqualified name to the definition module, as it already does for `push!`/`ACCESSED_ARTIFACTS`). Behavior-preserving.

## Pass 10 — quick documentation pass (typos + improvements, verified)

> **Status / provenance.** A quick, focused pass over **user-facing documentation and docstrings** (developer inline comments de-prioritized, per request): **4 finders** — the large guide pages, the front-door docs (README/NEWS/index) + smaller pages, `src/` docstrings, and `ext/` docstrings — each deduped against the ~258 already-documented doc findings, with a light verifier that rejects opinion-only style churn. **23 candidates → 13 confirmed new, 9 duplicates, 1 rejected.** No Julia executed. Focus was typos/grammar in user-facing prose and substantive documentation improvements (missing/incomplete docstrings, unclear/stale user-facing text, un-rendered API entries).
>
> **Headline:** one **high-value rendered-docs gap** — the flagship exported constructor `TimeVaryingInput` (and `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation`) are missing from the `inputs.md` `@docs` block, so their docstrings are never rendered on the docs site even though the page's prose documents them. Plus a handful of incomplete docstrings (undocumented keyword arguments) and minor grammar fixes in user-facing text.

### DOCS (Pass 10)

#### `docs/src/inputs.md`
- ⭐ **L295** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: high)_ — The API `@docs` block (L294-308) surfaces `SpaceVaryingInputs.SpaceVaryingInput` and many `TimeVaryingInputs` symbols (methods, BCs, `evaluate!`) but **omits `TimeVaryingInputs.TimeVaryingInput`** — the flagship exported constructor that the entire first half of the page documents (full docstring at `src/TimeVaryingInputs.jl:150`). Its signature/docstring is therefore never rendered on the docs site. Notably `evaluate!` (the other public-interface member) *is* listed, making the omission inconsistent. **Fix:** Add `ClimaUtilities.TimeVaryingInputs.TimeVaryingInput` to the `@docs` block (e.g. directly above the `SpaceVaryingInput` line).
- **L180** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` section (L165-180) ends with "For more information, please refer to the docstring", but `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` (full docstring at `src/TimeVaryingInputs.jl:239`) is **not** in any `@docs` block, so the referenced docstring is never rendered — a dangling cross-reference. **Fix:** Add `ClimaUtilities.TimeVaryingInputs.LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` to the `@docs` block (L294-308), and/or make the prose a live `[`LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation`](@ref)`.
- **L218** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — In the `TimeVaryingInput` usage example, the comment "In either cases, we can always call evolve_model(...)" is ungrammatical. **Fix:** "In either case" (or "In both cases"). _(In a user-facing docs example, not a developer comment.)_

#### `docs/src/regridders.md`
- **L10** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The intro bullet says `TempestRegridder` performs "conservative interpolation **onto** lat-long grids", which reverses the actual direction and contradicts L34 ("performs conservative interpolation **of** lat-lon grids **onto computational domains**"). A reader could wrongly conclude the output is a lat-lon grid rather than a `Field` on the `target_space`. **Fix:** Reword to match L34, e.g. "conservative interpolation of lat-lon grids onto the computational domain". The parallel `InterpolationsRegridder` phrasing at L15 ("interpolation onto lat-long(-z) and x-y-z grids") reads with the same reversed sense and should be adjusted too.

#### `docs/src/datastructures.md`
- **L35** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — "`get!` retrieves the value **associated to** the key" — the standard collocation is "associated **with**". **Fix:** "the value associated with the key".

#### `NEWS.md`
- **L104** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — The v0.1.22 note describing `ITime` says "a time type that does not **incur in** floating point errors"; "incur" is transitive and takes no preposition. **Fix:** "does not incur floating point errors" (remove "in"). _(Distinct from the already-logged L103 issue.)_

### SRC (Pass 10)

#### `src/TimeVaryingInputs.jl`
- **L252** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — In the public `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` docstring, a broken parallel construction: "...as first **filling** the years in between by performing linear interpolation across years, then **performs** a second linear interpolation for the specific day". "then performs" does not agree with the "first filling ... by performing" gerund structure. **Fix:** "then **performing** a second linear interpolation".

### EXT (Pass 10)

#### `ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl`
- **L83** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The `NCFileReader(file_paths, varname; preprocess_func, cache_max_size)` constructor docstring has a `## Argument` section (singular) that documents **only `file_paths`**. The user-facing keyword args `preprocess_func` (function applied to read data — e.g. unit conversion / NaN removal; default `identity`) and `cache_max_size` (LRU read-cache size, default 128), plus the positional `varname`, are undocumented, so users cannot discover them from the docstring. **Fix:** Rename the section to `## Arguments` and add bullets for `varname`, `preprocess_func`, and `cache_max_size`.

#### `ext/DataHandlingExt.jl`
- **L162** `[grammar]` _(severity: medium)_ — In the `DataHandler` constructor docstring, "if `varnames` is a vector with **the number of entries as** `file_paths`" is missing "same", making the multi-file mode-selection heuristic ambiguous/ungrammatical (it actually triggers when the counts are equal). **Fix:** "a vector with the **same** number of entries as `file_paths`".
- **L164** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — Same docstring, second mode: "we assume that each file contains all the variables and **is temporal chunk**" is missing an article. **Fix:** "...and **is a** temporal chunk".
- **L149** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — LRU-cache note in the same docstring: "increasing the cache size can lead to improved **performances**" (non-idiomatic plural). **Fix:** "improved performance".
- **L581** `[doc-error]` _(severity: low)_ — The `regridded_snapshot(data_handler, date)` docstring says "the `varnames` argument determines the order of arguments to the `compose_function`", but this method has **no `varnames` argument** — the ordering comes from the `varnames` given when the `DataHandler` was constructed. A reader may hunt for a nonexistent argument. **Fix:** Reword to reference the handler, e.g. "the order of `varnames` used to construct the `data_handler` determines the argument order passed to `compose_function`".

#### `ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl`
- **L67** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The `InterpolationsRegridder` constructor shows `interpolation_method = Interpolations.Linear()` in its signature, but the "Keyword arguments" section documents only `extrapolation_bc`, `dim_increasing`, and `dim_names` — `interpolation_method` is never described, so users cannot tell what values it accepts. **Fix:** Add a bullet: "`interpolation_method` — the gridded interpolation method from Interpolations.jl to use along each dimension (default `Interpolations.Linear()`)".

## Pass 11 — exhaustive documentation pass (verified; salvaged from interrupted run)

> **Status / provenance.** An exhaustive docs sweep: **18 finders** (one per major user-facing page, grouped for small ones; docstrings covered by 7 source-file-group finders; plus a `@docs`/`@ref` completeness specialist and a cross-doc terminology specialist), each deduped against the ~258 prior doc findings **plus Pass 10**. The run was **stopped mid-verification at the user's request**: all **18/18 finders completed** (141 candidates), and **130/141 candidates were verified** before the stop (11 unverified were excluded). Each surviving candidate carries **one verifier vote (Sonnet)** — lighter than the multi-round verification of earlier passes — so treat `low`/`trivial` items as strong leads rather than gospel. Of 112 verifier-confirmed items, **25 were dropped as collisions with already-documented lines** and within-file duplicates were merged, leaving **86 unique new findings**. No Julia executed (static-only).

> **Headline — 4 high-severity doc-errors** (runnable examples / setup docs that are wrong today):
> - `docs/src/regridders.md:53` — the `TempestRegridder(...)` example passes 4 positional args to a 3-positional constructor and never passes the **required** `regrid_dir` keyword → `MethodError`.
> - `docs/src/inputs.md:204` — the `TimeVaryingInput` example uses `zero(target_space)`, but ClimaCore has no `Base.zero(::Space)` (only `Fields.zeros(space)`) → `MethodError` if run.
> - `docs/src/filereaders.md:49` — a `!!! note` (repeated at L89-90) claims file order "does not matter", but `NCFileReader` **errors** unless the aggregated dates are sorted (`issorted(...)` guard).
> - `README.md:89` — describes a standalone `buildkite` environment, but `.buildkite/` holds only `pipeline.yml` (no `Project.toml`); CI reuses the `test` environment and layers CUDA/MPI via `Pkg.add` at runtime.

|---|---|---|---|---|

| SRC | 6 | 5 | 11 | **22** |
| EXT | 2 | 7 | 1 | **10** |

#### `README.md`
- **L36** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The README jumps straight from the feature list to contributor/developer guidelines. There is no 'Installation' section (e.g. `] add ClimaUtilities`) and no minimal quickstart code snippet showing how to actually use any of the listed modules. For the repo's front door, a first-time visitor has no runnable example or install instructions to try the package. **Fix:** Insert a short 'Installation' + 'Quickstart' section between the feature list and the Developer Guidelines heading, e.g. `] add ClimaUtilities` plus a few lines using one core feature (or at minimum a link to a docs quickstart page).
- **L75** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This claim is contradicted by the repo itself: `docs/Manifest.toml` is tracked in git (`git ls-files` lists it, with its own commit history), while `.gitignore` only excludes `/Manifest.toml` and `test/Manifest.toml`. So one of the four described environments (documentation) does check in its manifest, which this section doesn't mention. **Fix:** Either remove `docs/Manifest.toml` from version control to match the stated policy, or amend this section to note that the documentation environment's manifest is intentionally an exception (e.g., for reproducible doc builds).
- ⭐ **L89** `[doc-error]` _(severity: high)_ — This describes 'buildkite' as one of four standalone environments (with its own dependency set), but no such environment exists: `.buildkite/` contains only `pipeline.yml`, no `Project.toml`/`Manifest.toml`. Checking `.buildkite/pipeline.yml` shows every CI step actually runs with `--project=test`, and CUDA/MPI are added to that same `test` environment at CI runtime via `Pkg.add("CUDA")`/`Pkg.add("MPI")` in the init step. So there are really three environments (project, documentation, test), and 'buildkite' is not an independent one — this section is stale and will send contributors looking for files that don't exist. **Fix:** Rewrite this paragraph to say CI reuses the `test` environment (instantiated with `--project=test`) and layers `CUDA`/`MPI` onto it at runtime via `Pkg.add`, rather than describing 'buildkite' as a fourth, self-contained environment.
- **L125** `[doc-error]` _(severity: low)_ — 'TestEnv' does not match any name introduced earlier — the 'Tests and environments' section calls it the 'test' environment (lowercase), and 'TestEnv' appears nowhere else in the repo (checked via repo-wide grep). A reader following 'see previous section' will not find this term defined there. **Fix:** Change 'TestEnv' to 'test' to match the environment name used in the preceding section, or clarify if a distinct `TestEnv.jl` package is actually meant.

#### `docs/src/datahandling.md`
- **L12** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — "the various core tasks and features and split into other independent modules" is ungrammatical; the source docstring (src/DataHandling.jl:14) correctly reads "are split". **Fix:** Change "features and split" to "features are split".
- **L28** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This bullet describes both `previous_time` and `next_time` together but says the returned snapshot is always "before" the given time/date. `next_time` actually returns the snapshot AFTER the given time/date (see its own docstring in ext/DataHandlingExt.jl: "Return the time in seconds of the snapshot after the given time"). The module-level docstring in src/DataHandling.jl correctly uses "before/after" for this same sentence, but this guide page dropped the "/after", making the description factually incomplete/misleading for `next_time`. **Fix:** Change to "...to obtain the time of the snapshot before/after the given `time` or `date`." (or split into two separate bullets, one saying "before" for `previous_time` and one saying "after" for `next_time`).
- **L32** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — The last bullet in the "key functions" list ends without terminal punctuation before the next sentence starts, which reads as a run-on. **Fix:** Add a period: "...to read a particular snapshot."
- **L36** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This describes two separate inputs ("reference date" and "simulation starting time"), but the current `DataHandler` constructor only accepts a single unified `start_date` keyword; the old, separate `reference_date` and `t_start` keyword arguments are deprecated (`t_start` is now fully ignored — see ext/DataHandlingExt.jl lines 211-229) and both were folded into `start_date`. `time_to_date`'s own docstring confirms the formula uses only `start_date` (`date = start_date + time`). This sentence is stale wording left over from the pre-consolidation two-parameter API. **Fix:** Change to "Conversion between time and date is performed using the `start_date` provided to the `DataHandler`."
- **L76** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — This heading jumps straight from the page's level-1 title to level-4 (`####`) with no level-2/3 heading in between, and is inconsistent with the other top-level sections on the same page ("## Example: Linear interpolation of a single data variable", "## API", both level 2). Sibling documentation pages (filereaders.md, regridders.md, datastructures.md) all consistently nest h1 -> h2 -> h3. This mismatch will render the "Heuristics" heading unexpectedly small/nested in the generated documentation sidebar/TOC compared to surrounding sections. **Fix:** Change "####" to "##" so it matches the heading level of the other top-level sections on this page.
- **L86** `[typo]` _(severity: trivial)_ — "a list of list of files" should be "a list of lists of files" (consistent with the wording used for the same feature elsewhere, e.g. the `DataHandler` docstring's "It is a list of lists of paths to NetCDF files"). **Fix:** Change to "a list of lists of files".
- **L124** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The comment incorrectly attributes loading of the `DataHandling` extension to `ClimaCore` + `Interpolations`. Per the package's `[extensions]` table, `DataHandlingExt` is actually part of `ClimaUtilitiesClimaCoreNCDatasetsExt`, triggered by loading `ClimaCore` AND `NCDatasets` (this is even stated correctly in the admonition earlier on this same page: "This extension is loaded when loading `ClimaCore` and `NCDatasets` are loaded."). `Interpolations` instead triggers loading of `InterpolationsRegridder` (via `ClimaUtilitiesClimaCoreInterpolationsExt`), which is exactly what the very next comment on the following line already (correctly) says. So this comment duplicates/misattributes the wrong dependency. **Fix:** Change the comment to "# Loading ClimaCore and NCDatasets automatically loads DataHandling" and keep it after the `import NCDatasets` line (before `import Interpolations`).
- **L180** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The "Example appendix" code block reuses `unit_conversion_func`, which was only defined in the earlier, separate "Example: Linear interpolation" code block (line 131) and is never redefined here. A reader who copies just this appendix snippet (introduced under its own heading as if self-contained) will hit `UndefVarError: unit_conversion_func not defined`. It's also unclear why a precip-style `*1000` unit conversion is appropriate for a generic `u + v` sum in this appendix. **Fix:** Either redefine `unit_conversion_func` (or use `identity`) inside the appendix snippet, or add an explicit note that this example continues from the previous code block's scope.
- **L198** `[doc-improvement]` (missing docstring) _(severity: low)_ — `Base.close(data_handler::DataHandler)` has a public docstring ("Close all files associated to the given `data_handler`.") defined in ext/DataHandlingExt.jl, but it is not listed in this page's ```@docs``` block, so it never gets rendered in the generated documentation. Analogous per-module `close` methods ARE listed in the API sections of sibling pages (e.g. docs/src/filereaders.md lists `Base.close`, and docs/src/inputs.md lists `Base.close(::ClimaUtilities.TimeVaryingInputs.AbstractTimeVaryingInput)`). **Fix:** Add `Base.close(::ClimaUtilities.DataHandling.DataHandler)` to the ```@docs``` block so its docstring is rendered.

#### `docs/src/datastructures.md`
- **L62** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The API `@docs` block lists 12 Base-method extensions for `LRUCache` but omits three methods that also have full docstrings in src/DataStructures.jl: `Base.iterate` (source line 122), `Base.:(==)` (source line 108), and `Base.merge` (source line 258). None of these three is referenced by any `@docs` block anywhere else in docs/src/*.md either, so Documenter never renders them on the site. This is especially notable for `merge`, whose docstring explains that merging two `LRUCache`s intentionally throws an error — an important behavioral gotcha that is currently undiscoverable from the rendered docs. **Fix:** Add `Base.iterate`, `Base.:(==)`, and `Base.merge` to the `@docs` block in docs/src/datastructures.md so their docstrings are rendered on the page.

#### `docs/src/filereaders.md`
- **L17** `[doc-error]` _(severity: low)_ — The section heading (and the similar reference at line 61, "# Loading NCDatasets automatically loads `NCFileReaders`") uses the code-formatted name `NCFileReaders` (plural), but no such identifier exists anywhere in the codebase. The actual struct/constructor is the singular `NCFileReader` (ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl), and the extension module is `NCFileReaderExt`. **Fix:** Change both occurrences to the singular `NCFileReader`, e.g. the comment on line 61 could read "# Loading NCDatasets automatically loads the `NCFileReaderExt` extension".
- **L30** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This claim contradicts the actual implementation of `FileReaders.read`. On a cache hit the function executes `copy(file_reader._cached_reads[date])` (ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl:237) — a fresh allocation every single call, done specifically to avoid aliasing the cached array. On a cache miss it builds a brand-new array via broadcasting `preprocess_func.(...)` (lines 243-246, 259-261). No array is ever reused/preallocated across `read` calls; only the disk read is skipped on a cache hit, not the memory allocation. **Fix:** Reword, e.g.: "Cached reads are returned as a copy of the stored array, so repeated calls avoid re-reading from disk (though a new array is still allocated for each call)." Remove or correct the "without reallocating" claim.
- **L41** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The guide states the default cache size (128) but never mentions that it is configurable via the `cache_max_size` keyword argument of the `NCFileReader` constructor (`cache_max_size::Int = 128` in ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl), so readers have no way to discover how to tune cache size for their workload from the guide alone. **Fix:** Add a sentence such as: "This default can be changed by passing the `cache_max_size` keyword argument to `NCFileReader`."
- ⭐ **L49** `[doc-error]` _(severity: high)_ — This is factually wrong. NCDatasets' multi-file dataset (opened with `aggdim=...`, `deferopen=false`) concatenates files strictly in the order given in `file_paths` — it does not sort them by time (confirmed in CommonDataModel's `MFDataset` constructor, which builds `ds = DeferDataset.(TDS, fnames, mode; kwargs...)` preserving input order). `FileReaders.NCFileReader` then enforces `issorted(available_dates) || error("Cannot process files that are not sorted in time...")` (ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl ~line 158). So passing files out of chronological order causes construction to error, not "not matter." The same incorrect claim is repeated in the Example section at lines 89-90 ("While the order is not strictly required, it is still good practice to pass the files in the correct order."). **Fix:** Correct both occurrences, e.g.: "Files must currently be passed in chronological order — `NCFileReader` raises an error if the aggregated dates are not sorted."
- **L53** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The "## API" reference lists `read!`, and it is the actual mutating accessor (`read!(dest, file_reader, date)` in ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl), but the Example section only ever demonstrates the non-mutating `read` function. There is no working example anywhere in the guide showing how to call `read!` with a preallocated `dest` array, so users have no reference for that half of the documented API. **Fix:** Add a short snippet after the existing example, e.g.:

#### `docs/src/index.md`
- **L16** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The index.md 'Features' overview omits TimeManager/ITime entirely, even though README.md lists `TimeManager` as a core module (README L19), there is a dedicated timemanager.md guide, and ITime is one of the package's most prominent types. The feature list on the landing page therefore disagrees with the README module list and the guides, so a user browsing the overview would not discover TimeManager. **Fix:** Add a `### `TimeManager`` subsection to the Features list (e.g., after ClimaArtifacts) describing ITime, mirroring the README bullet, so the overview matches README.md and the timemanager.md guide.
- **L28** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — Missing article before `Field`; the same paragraph correctly says "map input to a `Field`" two sentences earlier, but this clause drops the article. **Fix:** "...to set the value of a `Field`"
- **L29** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — Subject-verb agreement: "`TimeVaryingInputs` implement" should be "`TimeVaryingInputs` implements" since it refers to a single module/type acting as the subject here (contrast with the earlier compound-subject sentence "`SpaceVaryingInputs` and `TimeVaryingInputs` provide functions...", which correctly uses the plural verb). **Fix:** "`TimeVaryingInputs` implements linear and nearest neighbor interpolations."
- **L30** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This is stale: src/TimeVaryingInputs.jl also defines a third interpolation method, `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` (used to remove diurnal/seasonal discontinuities when filling between yearly periods, and documented in docs/src/inputs.md), which is not mentioned here. The overview implies only two interpolation strategies exist. **Fix:** Either list all three (e.g. "...implement linear, nearest-neighbor, and linear-period-filling interpolations") or soften to "...implement several interpolation methods (see the Space and Time Inputs page for the full list)."
- **L74** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — `TimeManager` is a full module with its own dedicated page (docs/src/timemanager.md, listed in docs/make.jl's navigation) and exported public API (`to_datetime`, `strdate_to_datetime`, `datetime_to_strdate`, `trigger_callback`, `Monthly`, `EveryTimestep`), but index.md's "Features" section has no corresponding subsection for it — every other page in the nav (ClimaArtifacts, Space/TimeVaryingInputs, FileReaders, Regridders, OnlineLogging, OutputPathGenerator, DataHandling, DataStructures) is summarized here except TimeManager. A new user skimming the overview page for what ClimaUtilities offers would miss this feature entirely. **Fix:** Add a `### `TimeManager`` subsection (e.g. positioned after `OutputPathGenerator`, matching its place in make.jl's `pages` list) briefly describing its calendar/date-conversion utilities and callback-scheduling helpers (`Monthly`, `EveryTimestep`).

#### `docs/src/inputs.md`
- **L21** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — "This example" does not refer to any concrete code shown just above — the first actual code example on the page appears much later, at line 73 — so the phrase can confuse readers expecting a snippet at this point. **Fix:** Reword to something like "In short, `TimeVaryingInput` can take different types of inputs and be used with a single interface (`evaluate!`)."
- **L35** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The phrasing groups both kwargs under "underlying constructors in the `Regridder`", but per the `DataHandler` docstring (ext/DataHandlingExt.jl lines 190-193) `file_reader_kwargs` is passed to the file reader's constructor (e.g. `NCFileReader`), not the `Regridder`. The identical sentence is repeated verbatim at line 262 in the `SpaceVaryingInputs` section. **Fix:** Reword to, e.g., "It is possible to pass down keyword arguments to the underlying `Regridder` and file-reader constructors via `regridder_kwargs` and `file_reader_kwargs`, respectively." and apply the same fix at line 262.
- **L148** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — Awkward, backwards word order ("not ... only") makes the sentence hard to parse on first read. **Fix:** "In this sense, `PeriodicCalendar` is not only a true boundary condition." or "...is not solely a boundary condition."
- ⭐ **L204** `[doc-error]` _(severity: high)_ — The example builds an empty Field with `zero(target_space)`, but ClimaCore does not define `Base.zero` for a `Space` — only `Base.zeros(space)` / `Base.zeros(FT, space)` exist (ClimaCore.Fields), while `Base.zero` is only overloaded for an existing `Field`. Since the example only does `import ClimaCore` (not `using`), `zero(target_space)` resolves to the generic `Base.zero`, which has no method for a Space and throws a `MethodError` if actually run. **Fix:** Change the line to `albedo_field = ClimaCore.Fields.zeros(target_space)`.
- **L246** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — Redundant construction "loaded when loading ... is loaded" — this admonition is copy-pasted verbatim from line 11 (already flagged there) into the `SpaceVaryingInputs` section, repeating the same grammar defect at a second location. **Fix:** "This extension is loaded when `ClimaCore` is loaded."
- **L268** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The `@ref timevaryinginput` link only resolves to the top-level `## TimeVaryingInputs` header (`@id timevaryinginput`, line 9); the `### NetCDF file inputs` subsection it's meant to point readers to (line 39) has no explicit anchor of its own, so the link doesn't take the reader there directly. **Fix:** Add an explicit id, e.g. `### [NetCDF file inputs](@id netcdf-file-inputs)`, and change the cross-reference to `[@ref netcdf-file-inputs]`.
- **L294** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The API `@docs` block never renders `ClimaUtilities.TimeVaryingInputs.TimeVaryingInput` — the core constructor used in every single example on this page — nor `ClimaUtilities.TimeVaryingInputs.LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation`, which has its own dedicated prose subsection (line 165, "### `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation`") and by far the most detailed docstring in the module. Neither symbol is rendered anywhere else in the built docs (confirmed by scanning every `@docs` block in docs/src/*.md), so readers have no generated reference for their actual keyword arguments (start_date, regridder_type, regridder_kwargs, file_reader_kwargs, compose_function, period, etc.). **Fix:** Add `ClimaUtilities.TimeVaryingInputs.TimeVaryingInput` and `ClimaUtilities.TimeVaryingInputs.LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` to the `@docs` block in the API section.

#### `docs/src/onlinelogging.md`
- **L32** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — With the default `first_update_after_n_calls = 2`, `_update!` only starts recording once `wt.n_calls[] > 2` (src/OnlineLogging.jl lines 74-99), meaning the first TWO steps are ignored and the compensation/scaling happens on the THIRD recorded call, not on "the second step" as stated here. **Fix:** Reword to e.g. "...ignoring the first two steps and scaling the cost of the third step to compensate)."

#### `docs/src/outputpathgenerator.md`

#### `docs/src/regridders.md`
- **L21** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This is a no-target `@ref`, so Documenter resolves it by matching the link text ("`SpaceVaryingInputs` and `TimeVaryingInputs`") against a header. The intended target is the inputs.md page title, but that title reads "`SpaceVaringInputs` and `TimeVaryingInputs`" (typo: SpaceVaring). - ⭐ **L53** `[doc-error]` _(severity: high)_ — This example call passes 4 positional arguments, but the actual `TempestRegridder` constructor (ext/TempestRegridderExt.jl) only takes 3 positional arguments (`target_space`, `varname`, `input_file`) plus a required keyword argument `regrid_dir` (declared after `;`, no default). As written, "regrid_output" would bind to `varname`, "u" to `input_file", and "era5_example.nc" would be a 4th, unexpected positional argument, causing a MethodError; `regrid_dir` is never passed as a keyword even though it is mandatory. **Fix:** reg = Regridders.TempestRegridder(target_space, "u", "era5_example.nc"; regrid_dir = "regrid_output")
- **L86** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The FAQ heading is written at the same level (`##`) as "## InterpolationsRegridder" above it, rather than as a subsection of it. Because of this, the following "### Example" (line 96), which is a general `InterpolationsRegridder` construction/usage example unrelated to the z-extrapolation FAQ, ends up structurally nested under the FAQ heading in the document/TOC hierarchy instead of under "InterpolationsRegridder" where it belongs (mirroring the "### Example" that is correctly nested under "## TempestRegridder" earlier in the file). **Fix:** Demote the FAQ heading to `### FAQ: How do I enable linear extrapolation in z?` so it nests under "## InterpolationsRegridder", and/or move the generic "### Example" section to appear directly after the InterpolationsRegridder overview and before the FAQ.
- **L123** `[doc-improvement]` (missing docstring) _(severity: medium)_ — `Regridders.regrid!` (the allocation-free, in-place counterpart to `regrid`, fully documented with a docstring in ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl and stubbed in src/Regridders.jl alongside `regrid`) is never referenced by any `@docs` block in the documentation. Its docstring is therefore never rendered anywhere, so users have no way to discover this public API function from the docs site. **Fix:** Add `ClimaUtilities.Regridders.regrid!` to the `@docs` block in the "## API" section, after `ClimaUtilities.Regridders.regrid`.

#### `docs/src/timemanager.md`
- **L69** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — Passing the string literal "time1" as one of the @show arguments causes Documenter to render the literal line `"time1" = "time1"` in the built docs (since @show prints `expr = value` for each argument), which is confusing, meaningless output for readers rather than a helpful section label. **Fix:** Drop the "time1" argument (just `@show counter(time1) period(time1) epoch(time1) date(time1)`), or replace it with a prose sentence / `# time1` comment instead of embedding it in @show.

- **L193** `[grammar]` _(severity: trivial)_ — Number mismatch: plural "codes" paired with singular "simulation" reads awkwardly. **Fix:** "For typical code and simulations, we recommend..." (or "codes and simulations").
- **L197** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — "question on what" should be "question of what"; also "there are natural periods ... use it" has a number mismatch (plural "periods" referred to by singular "it"). **Fix:** "Regarding the question of what `period` to use: if there is a natural period (e.g., you are dealing with an hourly diagnostic variable), use it; otherwise you can stick with the default."

So why not use them directly?"
