- **L272** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — The sentence has a dangling construction / subject-verb mismatch: "Dates ... means" doesn't parse cleanly because "being part of the standard library" is attached to "Dates" as a participial phrase but then treated as the subject of "means". **Fix:** "Julia's `Dates` are not necessarily faster or better, and being part of the standard library means that it is hard to improve them."
- **L292** `[doc-improvement]` (missing docstring) _(severity: medium)_ — The exported TimeManager symbols `to_datetime`, `strdate_to_datetime`, `datetime_to_strdate`, `trigger_callback`, `Monthly`, and `EveryTimestep` (all defined with docstrings and exported from src/TimeManager.jl) are never listed in this `@docs` block or anywhere else in docs/src. Since docs/make.jl maps only this page to the TimeManager module and there is no `@autodocs` fallback, these public documented functions/types are completely absent from the built documentation site. **Fix:** Add entries for ClimaUtilities.TimeManager.to_datetime, .strdate_to_datetime, .datetime_to_strdate, .trigger_callback, .Monthly, and .EveryTimestep to the @docs block (or a new subsection) so their existing docstrings are actually rendered.
- **L300** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — Base.:(==)(t1::ITime, t2::Dates.DateTime), Base.:(%)(x::ITime, y::ITime), and Dates.DateTime(t::ITime) (src/ITime.jl) all carry proper docstrings but are not included in the @docs list, so those docstrings never render even though they describe important public behavior (equality with DateTime, `%` as an alias for `mod`, and DateTime conversion). **Fix:** Add Base.:(==)(t1::ClimaUtilities.TimeManager.ITime, t2::Dates.DateTime), Base.:(%)(x::ClimaUtilities.TimeManager.ITime, y::ClimaUtilities.TimeManager.ITime), and Dates.DateTime(t::ClimaUtilities.TimeManager.ITime) to the @docs block.

### SRC (Pass 11)

#### `src/ClimaArtifacts.jl`
- **L1** `[doc-improvement]` (missing docstring) _(severity: low)_ — The `ClimaArtifacts` module itself has no docstring, unlike the sibling modules covered in this same audit: `OutputPathGenerator` (module docstring at lines 1-5 of OutputPathGenerator.jl) and `TimeManager` (module docstring at lines 1-6 of TimeManager.jl). A one-line module description would improve consistency and give a quick orientation for anyone browsing the source (e.g. via `?ClimaUtilities.ClimaArtifacts`). **Fix:** Add a short module docstring above `module ClimaArtifacts`, e.g.: '"""\n    ClimaArtifacts\n\nThis module provides `@clima_artifact`, an MPI-safe way to access Julia artifacts (including lazily-downloaded ones) and to track which artifacts were used during a simulation.\n"""'

#### `src/DataHandling.jl`
- **L16** `[grammar]` _(severity: trivial)_ — "if need arises" is missing an article and reads ungrammatically. **Fix:** Change to "if the need arises" (or "if needed").
- **L22** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The overview list of "key functions" omits `regridded_snapshot!` (the in-place counterpart, also part of the public extension API in `extension_fns`), as well as `dt`, `time_to_date`, and `date_to_time`, all of which have their own docstrings in the extension but are not mentioned in this module-level summary, reducing discoverability. **Fix:** Add bullets for `regridded_snapshot!` (in-place version of `regridded_snapshot`) and briefly mention `dt`, `time_to_date`, `date_to_time` as time/date conversion helpers.
- **L30** `[typo]` _(severity: trivial)_ — Missing terminal punctuation: the sentence ending in "...to read a particular snapshot" runs directly into the next sentence "Most `DataHandling` functions..." with no period separating them. **Fix:** Add a period after "a particular snapshot."

#### `src/DataStructures.jl`
- **L11** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — Two factual errors in the module-level docstring. (1) `DataHandler` is not a module — it is the struct defined inside the `DataHandling` module (src/DataHandling.jl); the parallel phrasing with "`FileReaders` module" incorrectly implies `DataHandler` is a module. (2) The claim that the LRU cache stores "files that are currently open" is wrong: currently-open `NCDataset`s are tracked in a plain `Dict` (`const OPEN_NCFILES = Dict{...}()` in ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl), not an `LRUCache`. The `LRUCache` actually used there (`_cached_reads`) stores previously-read data arrays keyed by `DateTime`, not open file handles. **Fix:** "Within ClimaUtilities, the LRU cache is used by the `FileReaders` module (via its NCDatasets extension) to store previously-read data arrays, and by the `DataHandling` module to store regridded fields."
- **L124** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The `iterate` docstring only restates the generic Julia iteration protocol and never clarifies that, for this LRU cache, iteration simply delegates to `iterate(cache.cache)`/`iterate(cache.cache, state)` — i.e. the arbitrary order of the underlying `Dict`, not least-/most-recently-used order. A user could reasonably assume an `LRUCache` iterates in access-recency order. **Fix:** Add a note such as: "Elements are iterated in the (arbitrary) order of the underlying dictionary, not in order of last access."

#### `src/ITime.jl`
- **L173** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The docstring for `ITime(t; epoch = nothing)` never states the assumed unit of `t`. The implementation treats `t` as a number of seconds (it multiplies by 1e9 to get nanoseconds before dividing by the candidate period length), exactly like the sibling constructor `ITime(counter::Integer; period, epoch)`, whose docstring explicitly says "the function assumes that counter describes a time in seconds" — but this docstring omits that clarification, leaving the unit of `t` ambiguous to readers. **Fix:** Add a sentence such as: "`t` is assumed to represent a time interval in seconds." to match the sibling constructor's docstring.
- **L328** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The docstring implies ordinary range semantics, but the implementation (L334-337) returns a lazy `Base.Generator` comprehension, not an `AbstractRange`/array. Unlike a real range, the result cannot be indexed (e.g. `r[2]` fails) and isn't reusable the way a materialized range is; this distinction is not mentioned. **Fix:** Note explicitly that the return value is a lazy generator of `ITime` values (e.g. "Returns a generator of `ITime`s; use `collect` to materialize an array").

#### `src/OnlineLogging.jl`
- **L142** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — Subject-verb disagreement in the `!!! note` admonition of `report_walltime`'s docstring: "the number of steps become large" should be "becomes" since "number" is singular. **Fix:** ...until the number of steps becomes large.

#### `src/OutputPathGenerator.jl`
- **L78** `[grammar]` _(severity: trivial)_ — Missing definite article: 'returns path to the newly created folder' should be 'returns the path to the newly created folder'. **Fix:** Change 'returns path to the newly created folder' to 'returns the path to the newly created folder'.
- **L93** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — 'a `output_active`' should be 'an `output_active`' - the indefinite article should be 'an' before a word beginning with a vowel sound. (This is a second, separate occurrence of the same article mistake found a couple lines above at line 89-90.) **Fix:** Change 'a `output_active`' to 'an `output_active`'.

#### `src/TimeManager.jl`
- **L76** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The docstring states `EveryTimestep` is 'used to dispatch callback that is triggered every timestep', but no method of `trigger_callback` actually dispatches on `EveryTimestep` anywhere in the codebase - only `trigger_callback(..., ::Monthly, ...)` is defined. `EveryTimestep` is exported (line 16) as if it were a usable frequency option, but calling `trigger_callback(date_nextcall, date_current, EveryTimestep(), func, func_args)` throws a `MethodError`, directly contradicting the docstring's claim. **Fix:** Either implement a `trigger_callback(..., ::EveryTimestep, ...)` method (e.g. one that always calls `func` and returns `date_nextcall` unchanged), or update the docstring to state that `EveryTimestep` is not yet wired into `trigger_callback` / is reserved for future use, so users don't assume it is currently functional.
- **L85** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The phrase 'at time 00:00:00' is ambiguous. It is unclear whether it modifies 'next call date' (i.e., the next-call date is assumed to always be midnight) or describes when the comparison/invocation happens. The actual implementation does a plain `date_current >= date_nextcall` `DateTime` comparison with no special handling of any midnight/00:00:00 time component, so the phrase reads as an unexplained, dangling qualifier that could confuse readers about what guarantees the function provides regarding time-of-day. **Fix:** Reword for clarity, e.g.: 'If `date_current` is on or after `date_nextcall` (which is expected to be at 00:00:00, i.e. midnight), call the callback function and advance `date_nextcall` by one month.' or drop the '00:00:00' clause entirely if it isn't a real precondition enforced by the code.

#### `src/TimeVaryingInputs.jl`
- **L42** `[doc-error]` _(severity: low)_ — The `AbstractTimeVaryingInput` docstring's first sentence, taken at face value, says "`TimeVaryingInput`s" are implementation details, then two lines later lists `TimeVaryingInput(input; method, context)` as part of the public interface — an apparent self-contradiction. The intent (per the module-level comment) is that the concrete struct types like `AnalyticTimeVaryingInput` are implementation details, not the `TimeVaryingInput` constructor function itself, but the docstring's shorthand phrasing conflates the two. **Fix:** Reword to something like: "The concrete `*TimeVaryingInput` struct implementations (e.g. `AnalyticTimeVaryingInput`) should be considered implementation details. The exposed public interface is only ..." to avoid confusion with the `TimeVaryingInput` constructor.
- **L88** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The docstring states `repeat_date` is "required" when `period` is provided, but the `PeriodicCalendar` inner constructor (L124-133) only validates `period.value != 1`; it does not check that `repeat_date` is non-`nothing` when `period` is set. `PeriodicCalendar(Dates.Month(1), nothing)` therefore constructs successfully, contradicting the documented requirement, and any failure would surface later/deeper in extension code that assumes `repeat_date` is a real date whenever `period` is set. **Fix:** Either add validation in the constructor for this requirement, or clarify in the docstring that this pairing is not validated at construction time and misuse can lead to confusing errors downstream.
- **L163** `[grammar]` _(severity: low)_ — Extraneous article "a" before the two-item list "`times` and `vals`" is grammatically incorrect. **Fix:** "When `times` and `vals` are passed, ..."
- **L263** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` docstring presents `Day(1)` as an ordinary, equally-valid example for `period` (alongside `Year(1)`), but the constructor a few lines below (L314-315) explicitly warns `@warn("Only `period = Year(1)` has been tested, check results!")` for any period other than `Year`. The docstring gives no indication that `Day(1)` (or anything but `Year(1)`) is untested/experimental, so a user following the documented example would be misled about reliability. **Fix:** Add a caveat next to the `Day(1)` example, e.g.: "Note: only `period = Year(1)` has been thoroughly tested; other periods such as `Day(1)` will trigger a warning and results should be checked carefully."
- **L266** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The `LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation` docstring never mentions two hard constraints enforced by its own constructor: (1) `bc isa PeriodicCalendar` raises `error("LinearPeriodFillingInterpolation is incompatible with PeriodicCalendar")` (L316-318), and (2) `period.value == 1 || error("Only simple periods are supported (e.g., Year(1))")` (L312-313) rejects compound periods like `Year(2)`. A user reading only the docstring would not know these combinations are disallowed. **Fix:** Document both constraints, e.g.: "`extrapolation_bc` cannot be a `PeriodicCalendar` (an error is raised if it is). `period` must satisfy `period.value == 1` (e.g. `Year(1)`, `Month(1)`); compound periods such as `Year(2)` are rejected."

#### `src/Utils.jl`
- **L10** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — The implementation calls `searchsortedfirst(a, x)`, which requires `a` to be sorted in ascending order for correct results, but this precondition is never stated. On an unsorted `a` the function silently returns a meaningless index instead of erroring. **Fix:** Add: "`a` must be sorted in ascending order." (optionally add `# Arguments`/`# Returns` sections for consistency with `isequispaced`).
- **L29** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: medium)_ — `linear_interpolation` calls `searchsortedfirst(indep_vars, indep_value)`, so `indep_vars` must be sorted in ascending order for correct behavior, but this precondition is never documented. The docstring also lacks `# Arguments`/`# Returns` sections, unlike `isequispaced` elsewhere in the same file. **Fix:** State that `indep_vars` must be sorted in ascending order, and add `# Arguments`/`# Returns` sections describing each parameter and the returned value.
- **L251** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The implementation requires at least two dates to fall within the identified period (`length(dates_in_period) >= 2 || error("$(target_date) not in given dates for given period")`), but this failure mode is not mentioned anywhere in the docstring. **Fix:** Document the error condition, e.g.: "Throws an error if fewer than two dates in `dates` fall within the period containing `target_date`."
- **L344** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The implementation requires `period.value == 1` and throws `error("Only simple periods (e.g., \`Year(1)\`) are supported")` otherwise (e.g. `unique_periods(dates, Year(2))` errors), but this restriction is never mentioned in the docstring, so users can only discover it by reading the source or hitting the runtime error. **Fix:** Add: "Only unit periods (e.g. `Year(1)`, `Month(1)`) are supported; calling with a non-unit period such as `Year(2)` raises an error."

### EXT (Pass 11)

#### `ext/DataHandlingExt.jl`
- **L71** `[typo]` _(severity: low)_ — The field docstring for `dimensions` says 'long/lat', but every other place in the codebase that documents the same physical dimensions (e.g. ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl:45 'lon/lat', ext/DataHandlingExt.jl:42 'lat/lon', src/SpaceVaryingInputs.jl:13 'lat/lon') uses 'lon'. This is the only occurrence of 'long' and reads like a typo for 'lon'. **Fix:** Change 'long/lat' to 'lon/lat' for consistency with the rest of the documentation.
- **L92** `[doc-improvement]` _(severity: low)_ — The `preallocated_read_data` field docstring says 'storing read dataset' (singular), but the field is actually a `Dict{<:AbstractString, <:AbstractArray}` mapping each variable name in `varnames` to its own preallocated array (see `PR <: AbstractDict{<:AbstractString, <:AbstractArray}` at line 60 and its construction at lines 373-376). The current wording is grammatically awkward and doesn't convey that it's a per-variable dictionary of buffers, not a single dataset buffer. **Fix:** Reword to: "Dictionary mapping each variable name to preallocated memory for storing that variable's read data."
- **L406** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The `available_times` docstring describes the measurement as relative to 'the starting time of the simulation and the reference date' — two separate concepts. But the current public API has only a single `start_date` field/keyword (the old two-parameter model of `reference_date` + `t_start` was deprecated in this same file, see the `reference_date`/`t_start` depwarns around lines 212-229). The actual computation (`period_to_seconds_float.(available_dates .- start_date)`, line 305) uses only `start_date`. Using the stale term 'reference date' here is confusing/misleading since it implies a second, independent quantity that no longer exists as public API. **Fix:** Reword to: "Return the time in seconds of the snapshots in the data, measured relative to `start_date`."

#### `ext/InterpolationsRegridderExt.jl`
- **L82** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This statement is incorrect for the exact case it calls out as "particularly important": Z-only target spaces. For a Z-only space, `dim_increasing` has length 1 (matching the 1D target space, e.g. `(true,)`), but per the `regrid` implementation (lines 171-207), `dim_names` must have as many entries as the raw input data (e.g. 3, for lon/lat/z) so that `findfirst(name -> name in z_names, regridder.dim_names)` can locate the vertical dimension among all input dimensions. So `dim_increasing[i]` does NOT correspond to `dim_names[i]` in this scenario — `dim_names` indexes the original 3D input dimensions while `dim_increasing` indexes only the (already-reduced) 1D target space dimension. **Fix:** Clarify separately: "`dim_names` must have one entry per dimension of the raw input data. For non-Z-only spaces, `dim_increasing[i]` corresponds to `dim_names[i]`. For Z-only spaces receiving 3D input data, `dim_names` is used only to locate the vertical dimension among the input's dimensions and its length may differ from `dim_increasing`, which always matches the (1D) target space."

#### `ext/NCFileReaderExt.jl`
- **L216** `[grammar]` _(severity: trivial)_ — The `close_all_ncfiles` docstring reads 'Close all the `NCFileReader` currently open', which is missing pluralization since the function closes potentially many NCFileReader-backed datasets (it iterates over all of `OPEN_NCFILES`). **Fix:** Reword to: "Close all the currently open NetCDF files tracked across `NCFileReader`s." (or simply "Close all currently open NCFileReaders.")

#### `ext/SpaceVaryingInputsExt.jl`
- **L132** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The docstring's method signature shows `regridder_type::Symbol` as a required keyword argument with no default, but the actual method (a few lines below, `function SpaceVaryingInputs.SpaceVaryingInput(file_paths, varnames, target_space; regridder_type = nothing, ...)`) makes it optional with default `nothing` (which later falls back to `Regridders.default_regridder_type()`). A user reading only the docstring would incorrectly think this keyword is mandatory. **Fix:** Change the signature line to `regridder_type = nothing,` (or document `regridder_type::Union{Nothing,Symbol} = nothing`) and add a sentence noting that when omitted, the default regridder type is used.

#### `ext/TempestRegridderExt.jl`
- **L28** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The TempestRegridder docstring's "Implicit assumptions" list says the time dimension must be named "time" or "date", but the actual implementation used by this same extension (read_available_dates in nc_common.jl, included via `include("nc_common.jl")` at the top of this file) checks for "time", "t", "valid_time", and finally "date" (in that order). The docstring is stale/incomplete and omits two of the four supported names. **Fix:** Update the bullet to: "- the time dimension, if available, is called \"time\", \"t\", \"valid_time\", or \"date\" (checked in that order)".

#### `ext/time_varying_inputs_linearperiodfilling.jl`
- **L6** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The summary line states the difference is computed 'from `date_right` to `date_left`', but the implementation computes `beginningofperiod(date_right) - beginningofperiod(date_left)`, i.e. the difference FROM `date_left` TO `date_right` (using the usual 'B - A is the difference from A to B' convention). This is confirmed by the rest of the same docstring: '18/08/1995 (date_left) + 2 years is in `period_right`' shows the offset is added to date_left to reach date_right, not the reverse. The opening sentence has the direction backwards relative to the rest of the docstring and the code. **Fix:** Change to: "Return the difference in periods (in `Dates.Period`) from `date_left` to `date_right`." so it matches both the implementation and the explanatory example that follows.
- **L147** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — This example reuses `dates_period_left` (defined earlier as `[DateTime(1985, 1, 15), DateTime(1985, 2, 17), DateTime(1985, 12, 11)]`) as the *second* (dates_period_right) argument. Tracing the actual algorithm with these inputs gives `largest_first_date = max(1985-01-01, 1985-01-15) = 1985-01-15`, not the `1985-01-08` shown on the next line. If the second argument is instead the previously-defined `dates_period_right` (`[DateTime(1995,1,8), DateTime(1995,2,18), DateTime(1995,12,18)]`), the computation correctly yields `(1985-01-08, 1985-12-11)`, matching the documented output exactly. **Fix:** Replace the second argument with `dates_period_right`: `_interpolable_range([DateTime(1985, 1, 1), DateTime(1985, 12, 11)], dates_period_right, period)`.
- **L150** `[doc-error]` _(severity: medium)_ — The second argument mixes years 1995 and 1985 (`DateTime(1995, 1, 3)` and `DateTime(1985, 12, 21)`). The function itself validates `length(unique(beginningofperiod.(dates_period_right, period))) != 1` and throws `error("dates in dates_period_right belongs to different periods")` for exactly this kind of input, so this call would actually raise an error rather than return the value shown on the next line. Moreover, even after fixing the years to be consistent, the claimed result `DateTime(1985, 1, 3)` is smaller than `minimum(dates_period_left) == DateTime(1985, 1, 15)`, which is mathematically impossible since the first returned value is a `maximum(...)` that includes `minimum(dates_period_left)` as one of its operands — so the claimed output cannot be produced by this function with the given `dates_period_left`. **Fix:** Fix the inconsistent years in the second argument (e.g. both should be 1995, matching the pattern of the other examples) and recompute/verify the actual expected output rather than the currently-shown `[DateTime(1985, 1, 3), DateTime(1985, 12, 21)]`, which is not reachable given `dates_period_left = [DateTime(1985,1,15), DateTime(1985,2,17), DateTime(1985,12,11)]`.
